| D11 | Auto-login for `openclaw` (step 1 sub-item) | Enable auto-login for `openclaw` | **Cannot enable** — Tahoe enforces mutual exclusivity between FileVault and auto-login. Keeping FileVault ON (spec requirement), accepting that reboots require manual user login at the Mini's screen (Tailscale/SSH don't come up pre-login in this config, tested empirically 2026-04-21). | Spec requires FileVault. Disabling it would be the bigger spec deviation. Threat model: Mac Mini holds Gmail OAuth, API keys, Hylean credentials — disk encryption is meaningful protection against physical theft. Classical auto-login is convenience for a rare event (unplanned reboot while Peter away). Chose spec-compliance + encryption over convenience. | **On unplanned reboot (power cut) while Peter away, agents stay offline until someone logs in at the Mini.** Mitigations: (a) UPS recommended to eliminate flicker risk, (b) auto-update disabled to avoid surprise reboots, (c) can ask Olga or nanny to log in if away long, (d) **reversible in minutes** on Apple Silicon — if power cuts become a real pain point, revisit and disable FileVault + enable auto-login + move secrets to Keychain. Action item: Peter to consider UPS purchase (£50-80). |
| D12 | Agent naming registers (§2.2 line 140) | Per-agent direction "PA — female, French; ProA — female, British (Miranda calibration); CoS — male, German or Swiss" | **Marie (PA, French ✓) / Charlotte (ProA, British ✓) / Patrick (CoS, Anglo-Irish, off-spec on Germanic) / Sophie (pre-existing).** Also: first-name only across team, no surnames-of-record. | Two reasons. (1) **Patrick over Germanic for CoS** — Peter raised Patrick unprompted in the candidate discussion ("alternative Patrick"); §2.2 explicitly frames per-role direction as "inspiration, not binding"; Patrick has cleaner phonetic distinctness vs Marie (P/M) than Max would (M/M collision). Germanic option reserved as soft note for Research naming (week 4-6 build) where the architecture leaves nationality unspecified and a Mathematics+CS-rigor archetype reads naturally Germanic. (2) **First-name only across team** — Peter raised the deception risk (surnames imply human staff member; recipients may infer staff where the AI disclosure should be explicit) and the email-construction usability problem (`isabella.foxwood@fedchenkov.com` 7 syllables vs `izzy@fedchenkov.com` 2). First-name only resolves both at once: clean emails (`marie@`, `charlotte@`, `patrick@`, `sophie@`) and a posture that reads as "AI assistant" rather than "human staff" without forcing the deception question. Architecture §2.2 ("Bot display names = agent's actual name") is silent on surnames-of-record — neither requires nor forbids. Choice is consistent with §2.2 intent (real-people-feel) without implying human-staff confusion. | **Operational rules going forward:** (1) every external email from PA/ProA/CoS includes an AI-disclosure footer — exact wording to be authored at session 6b USER-VOICE-GUIDE.md update (e.g., "Marie is Peter Fedchenkov's AI assistant — please reply directly to Peter for anything sensitive or final"). (2) If a specific external context demands signature gravitas (ProA writing to a banking MD), the agent can sign as "Charlotte from Peter Fedchenkov's office" or "Charlotte W." inline without us provisioning a surname-of-record — optionality preserved. (3) Telegram bot display names = first names. @usernames are public + irreversible per BotFather; surface fallback patterns at step 9 BotFather session. (4) Research naming (week 4-6) revisit Germanic candidates (Stefan, Lukas) in fresh context. **Owner:** me — D12 captured at session close. | D16 | gog refresh-token storage backend | Plan-doc Phase B finding said "credentials in macOS Keychain on our setup" | **Empirical reality at 6a.17 Phase E1:** gogcli 0.14.0 supports three keyring backends — `auto` (default; resolves to platform best — macOS Keychain on Tahoe), `keychain` (force macOS Keychain), `file` (gogcli-managed JWE-encrypted files at `~/Library/Application Support/gogcli/keyring/`). Selected via `GOG_KEYRING_BACKEND=file` env var. **D16 = chose `file` backend over Keychain.** Reasons: (1) cron/SSH-friendly: file backend uses `GOG_KEYRING_PASSWORD` env var as encryption key — works in any process context where openclaw can read its own home dir. Resolves Q-Cron-Keychain-headless from STEP-11-12-GMAIL-CALENDAR-PLAN.md cleanly: "we don't use Keychain." Keychain backend would require GUI login session for unlock or `security unlock-keychain` ceremony, fragile in cron context. (2) Architecturally consistent with rest of openclaw secret stack: `openclaw.json` plaintext + 0600 staff (bot tokens); `~/.openclaw/credentials/*.json` plaintext + 0600 staff (gog client_secret, Marie allowFrom, etc.). gog file backend layers JWE encryption on top of FileVault baseline — *better* than rest of stack at-rest, not worse. (3) D7 non-admin posture: openclaw user has no GUI session under FileVault baseline (D11); auto-login disabled; SSH-only access. Keychain unlock-on-login behaviour assumes GUI login that doesn't happen. (4) D15 keychain recreate at 6a.17 added ACL friction: fresh keychain via `security create-keychain` has restrictive ACL that gog couldn't write to (verified empirically — first OAuth attempt failed with "Secret not found in keyring (refresh token missing)" symptom-not-cause readback after silent ACL-denied write). | **Implementation:** (a) Generated 32-byte random base64 password `~/.openclaw/credentials/gog-keyring-password` (mode 0600 staff, 45 bytes incl. newline, file_sha12 `2a03229ec270`). (b) Stored same password in 1Password vault `OpenClaw` Note `OpenClaw — gog keyring master password` (concealed field `gog_keyring_password`). (c) Appended to `~/.zshrc` (351 bytes / sha12 `b8c69acaa15f`): `export GOG_KEYRING_BACKEND=file` + `export GOG_KEYRING_PASSWORD="$(cat ~/.openclaw/credentials/gog-keyring-password 2>/dev/null)"` — env_var loaded from file on shell startup (44 chars, newline-stripped, env_sha12 `1b20561a11e2`). (e) Storage shape per E1 empirical: 3 keyring files written for one OAuth flow, all base64-encoded JWE envelopes (first 4 bytes `eyJh` = `{"a` decoded), all mode 0600 staff: `_gogcli_key_v1_dG9rZW46<email>` (per-account, ~1478 bytes), `_gogcli_key_v1_dG9rZW46default:<email>` (per-client+account, ~1493 bytes), `_gogcli_key_v1_dG9rZW4tc3ViOmRlZmF1bHQ6<google_sub_id>` (per-Google-sub-id, ~1505 bytes). | D20 | F45 gateway restoration ceremony | `launchctl bootstrap` + `kickstart` pair, runnable from SSH (with optional pfedchenkov admin escalation per opener) | Screen-Sharing-driven `openclaw gateway install --force --port 18789` + `openclaw gateway start` from openclaw GUI Terminal | macOS gui/502 launchd domain is GUI-session-bound, not user-bound — cannot bootstrap from SSH (with or without sudo-asuser bridging). Both opener's Path A (managed verb from SSH) and Path B (manual launchctl from SSH or pfedchenkov sudo) failed with `125: Domain does not support specified action / requires logged-in macOS GUI session for this user (gui/502)`. Empirically confirmed via 2 SSH attempts before pivoting to Screen Sharing. **Architectural conclusion**: macOS gui/<uid> launchd domains are bound to the active GUI login session for that uid, not just the uid existing on the system. Modern macOS (Catalina onward) hardens this boundary; `launchctl asuser` from sudo non-GUI context cannot bind to gui/<uid>. | F45 closed cleanly via Screen Sharing path. | F10 | Tahoe GUI password reset silently fails for SecureToken-enabled users (added 2026-04-24) | When resetting another user's password via System Settings → Users & Groups → ⓘ → Reset Password, with both admin and target user SecureToken-enabled, Tahoe's GUI appears to accept the new password but leaves the underlying auth subsystems desynced. Symptom: neither SSH login nor `su - <user>` accepts the new password. Root cause: GUI wrapper short-circuits some of the SecureToken/APFS/FileVault sync steps that `sysadminctl` performs correctly. Encountered at Session 6a.1 step 6.1 when resetting the openclaw account password that was never saved to 1Password at creation time. | Use `sudo sysadminctl -resetPasswordFor <user> -newPassword - -adminUser <admin> -adminPassword -` (all `-` flags for interactive prompts — nothing in shell history). Apple's supported programmatic API, handles the SecureToken chain atomically. Do NOT follow with a GUI reset — it can re-trigger the same desync. Save the new password to 1Password **before** testing login. Document for any future password-reset in DEVIATIONS-LOG operational-lessons. |
| F11 | Bundled skills auto-load by default — posture violation risk (added 2026-04-24) | OpenClaw 2026.4.22 auto-activates ALL 53 bundled skills wherever their corresponding CLI binary exists on the host. Paraphrased from WenHao Yu's bundled-skill writeup (verified against current docs.openclaw.ai): "it's not 'nothing unless installed' but 'everything unless disabled'." Without explicit `skills.allowBundled` whitelist in `openclaw.json`, skills like `apple-notes` (full Notes access), `himalaya` (IMAP/SMTP), and others activate silently. Violates §4.1 non-negotiable #6 ("No unreviewed ClawHub skills") if bundled is interpreted liberally — more importantly, violates the spirit of least-privilege. The §1.3 spec named 5 Day 1 skills; 4 are bundled-core, 1 is third-party (context-anchor, reviewed clean at 6.2a). **The named 5 are the only bundled skills we've reviewed and approved.** Everything else must be explicitly disabled. | At step 6.5, add to `openclaw.json`: `skills: { allowBundled: ["gog", "summarize", "obsidian", "github"] }` at the agents.defaults level (global baseline), with per-agent `agents.list[].skills: [...]` narrowing further. Full bundled-skill catalogue survey (the "53 bundled skills" review §1.3 requires) deferred to Session 6a.2 as its first task — done ahead of 6.3 so findings feed directly into the `allowBundled` list we paste into config. If set, only bundled skills in the list are eligible (managed/workspace skills unaffected)." WenHao's own config example confirms `{ "skills": { "allowBundled": [...] } }` at root. (2) Per Peter's decision at 6.2b, per-agent `agents.list[].skills` narrowing is NOT used — Day 1 runs global scope (same skill list visible to all 9 agents) because the real security boundaries are Docker sandbox (§4.1) + per-agent OAuth token scoping, not skill visibility. Owner: me at 6a.7. **CLOSED-SUBSTANTIVE 2026-04-27 at Session 6a.7-6a.8 step 7.8 + 7.10. Closure narrative written deliberately, not rushed.** The substantive forensics need (gateway log persistence across reboot for incident review) was MET FROM DAY ONE by `~/.openclaw/logs/gateway.log` and `~/.openclaw/logs/gateway.err.log` — the launchd-plist-managed stdout/stderr capture, redirected via `StandardOutPath` and `StandardErrorPath` keys in `~/Library/LaunchAgents/ai.openclaw.gateway.plist`. Confirmed at 6a.8 by `launchctl print gui/502/ai.openclaw.gateway`: `stdout path = /Users/openclaw/.openclaw/logs/gateway.log` and `stderr path = /Users/openclaw/.openclaw/logs/gateway.err.log`. Both files exist, are populated (6334 bytes plist-stdout end of 6a.7, growing across the 6a.8 bootout/bootstrap cycle), and survive reboot. Neither 6a.6 nor 6a.7 noticed they existed. **Investigation at 6a.7 wrongly framed F12 as "redirect launchd plist stdout/stderr"** — plist already did that correctly the whole time. The ONLY piece going to `/tmp/openclaw/openclaw-YYYY-MM-DD.log` was the bundled pino-style JSON-line file logger (resolved through `getResolvedLoggerSettings()` → `tmp-openclaw-dir-CWQcmOLf.js` resolver hardcoded to `/tmp/openclaw/`). This is supplementary structured-log output, not the primary forensics channel. **Investigation at 6a.7 found a top-level `logging` schema key** (sibling of `gateway`, not under `.properties.gateway.properties` where 6a.6 looked) with `logging.{level, file, maxFileBytes, consoleLevel, consoleStyle, redactSensitive, redactPatterns}` sub-schema. Edit applied at 6a.7: `.logging = {file: "/Users/openclaw/.openclaw/logs/gateway/gateway.log", maxFileBytes: 52428800}`. F17 hygiene held (stage in `~/.openclaw/openclaw.json.new`, mv-rename within same dir, chmod 600 + chgrp staff in same script block). Pre-edit canonical SHA `6b8dedc2…` matched in CFG and NEW (no agents.list drift). Live config grew 4422 → 4537 bytes (+115). New log dir pre-created at `~/.openclaw/logs/gateway/` (mode 0700 staff). **Edit was HOT-RELOAD same-PID 89749** (see F18 v4 update). Post-edit: `live==.last-good: True`, gateway state=active, `openclaw gateway status` reports `File logs: ~/.openclaw/logs/gateway/gateway.log` (the status surface honours the override). **But the daemon's actual file writer ignores `logging.file` — confirmed empirically at 6a.8 by full bootout/bootstrap cycle (PID 89749 → 98076).** Fresh process started today, no cache to fail to invalidate, full config re-read on init. Plist-stdout `gateway.log` line at 09:01:06.891 explicitly states `[gateway] log file: /tmp/openclaw/openclaw-2026-04-27.log` — daemon believes its log file is in /tmp despite `logging.file` being set. New path `~/.openclaw/logs/gateway/gateway.log` STILL does not exist after the bootstrap + `openclaw devices list` trigger. /tmp file grew 25209 → 37697 bytes (+12488) from device-list invocation. **Conclusion:** schema field `logging.file` is either unimplemented in the bundled logger init path, or scoped to mean something different from its description. The status surface (`openclaw gateway status`) reads `logging.file` from config but the file logger (pino transport configured at process boot) computes its path through a separate resolver that ignores the override. **Decision: leave `logging.file` config in place** as future-proofing (115 bytes of harmless config) — if OpenClaw fixes the implementation in a future release, our config is already prepared and the new path will start receiving writes; we'd notice on first `ls ~/.openclaw/logs/gateway/`. Reverting would require another hot-reload cycle for no real benefit. **F12 net status:** substantive concern (reboot-persistent gateway logs) was met by plist-managed `~/.openclaw/logs/gateway.log` from day one. The /tmp bundled-logger output is supplementary, ephemeral by design, acceptable to lose on reboot. The schema-vs-implementation gap is a documented finding, not a blocker. 7.10 SSH stop test confirmed plist-stdout persists across bootout/bootstrap cycle. F12 closes after 3 sessions of investigation that taught us the launchd plist had been doing the right thing the whole time. **6a.13 sub-fact correction:** F12 closure narrative captured the active gateway log path as `~/.openclaw/logs/gateway/gateway.log` (matching the unimplemented `logging.file` config-side declaration at 6a.7). Reality empirically observed at 6a.13 step 9.3-prelude (during channels-add forensics): plist redirects stdout/stderr to `~/.openclaw/logs/gateway.log` and `~/.openclaw/logs/gateway.err.log` — one level UP from the `gateway/` subdirectory, no `gateway/` segment. The empty `~/.openclaw/logs/gateway/` subdirectory is leftover scaffolding from 26 Apr (last-modified date confirms) and stays empty across all gateway lifecycle events. F12 closure substantive concern (reboot-persistent gateway logs) still met by plist-managed paths; the path-segment correction does NOT unwind F12 itself. Two log files surfaced at 6a.13 with distinct purposes: `gateway.log` for state/lifecycle (reload events, plugin lifecycle, agent-runner registration), `gateway.err.log` for security/audit (every CLI scope-upgrade WS-1008 event with `client=cli` vs `client=gateway-client` metadata, role/scope diffs, plus reload classifier WARN-lines like `[reload] config change requires gateway restart (X)`). Plus `config-audit.jsonl` and `config-health.json` in same dir — supplementary surfaces, not yet inspected. **Operational implication for step 15 cron/healthcheck:** parser must tail BOTH `gateway.log` AND `gateway.err.log` — restart-trigger classifier lines land in err.log, not the main log. | F14 | ~~`openclaw onboard` wizard 2026.4.22 emits a markdown-formatted deny entry~~ **REVISED 2026-04-25 at Session 6a.3 step 6.5.2: chat-client display artefact, NOT a wizard bug** | **Original report (2026-04-25 at 6.5.0):** Repeated read-backs (`cat | jq`, `grep sms`) showed `gateway.nodes.denyCommands` last entry as `"[sms.search](http://sms.search)"` — markdown auto-link form. Logged as F14 wizard bug. **Correction (2026-04-25 at 6.5.2):** During the staged-file workflow the same byte-string showed length 32 (broken form) on every display path until a SHA-256 readback was attempted. The hash check showed both LIVE (`~/.openclaw/openclaw.json`) and STAGED (`/tmp/openclaw.json.new`) last-entries matching SHA `be73a18f15037fbd`, length 10 — i.e., plain `"sms.search"`. The wizard wrote the correct 10-character token to disk. Something in the read path between SSH stdout and the chat session was rewriting any TLD-shaped dotted string (e.g. `sms.search`, where `.search` is a real gTLD) into a markdown auto-link before it reached me. The same chat layer also rewrote my output references like `/tmp/openclaw.json.new` into `[/tmp/openclaw.json.new](http://openclaw.json.new)` in the diff captures, which is the smoking-gun pattern. **Net effect:** F14 was never an OpenClaw bug. The deny list as wizard-generated is correct. No upstream report needed. **Operational lesson for future sessions:** when a JSON value's textual form looks suspiciously like an auto-linked URL after copy-paste, verify with display-immune checks (`len()`, `sha256`, byte-count, `od`) before logging a flag. The Tahoe Terminal → SSH → tmux → clipboard → chat-app pipeline has a long history of mangling specific patterns. | None — closed. Operational lesson captured in DEVIATIONS-LOG operational-notes section (TBD if we add one). **F14 lesson v2 (added 2026-04-25 at Session 6a.4 step 6.5.4 — REINFORCED):** the chat-display rewriting also affects (a) `diff` output that contains TLD-shaped tokens — saw `IDENTITY.md` rendered as `[IDENTITY.md](http://IDENTITY.md)` in a `diff <(jq ...)` capture even when the bytes on disk were clean; and (b) **commands themselves** when sent to Peter to copy-paste — `jq '...["IDENTITY.md"]...'` rendered with linkified strings inside the command, which would have written corrupted bytes to disk had the command been pasted as displayed (we caught it on the staging-file diff before mv). **Standard verification pattern moving forward:** for any edit involving dotted-TLD-shaped values (`*.md`, `*.search`, `*.io`, `*.new`, etc.), pre-compute clean reference SHA-256 prefixes and lengths in a code-execution sandbox where chat can't pollute, then have Peter run a `python3` block that reads the live file and emits SHA/len for each value — compare against the sandbox-computed references. SHA hex and integer lengths are display-immune (no dots or words for the rewriter to grab). **Defensive command construction:** when issuing shell commands to Peter that reference dotted basenames, use shell variables (`A=AGENTS; EXT=md; cat "${A}.${EXT}"`) or wildcards (`*.md`, `find -name '*HOOK*'`) so chat never sees a clean dotted-TLD token. `jq --arg p1 "${I}.${EXT}"` is the right construction for JSON edits — variable expansion happens in the shell at exec time, jq receives the joined string, and chat-display sees only `${VAR}.${EXT}` placeholders. |

| F17 | `mv` from `/tmp` regresses file mode and group on the openclaw config (added 2026-04-25 at Session 6a.3 step 6.5.2) | When applying the §4.1 edit at 6.5.2, the workflow staged the new config at `/tmp/openclaw.json.new`, validated JSON, then `mv`-ed it into `~/.openclaw/openclaw.json`. **Result:** the live file's previous metadata (mode `0600`, group `staff`) was REPLACED by the staging file's metadata (mode `0644`, group `wheel`) — i.e. the file briefly became world-readable, including the 48-character gateway auth token. macOS `mv` preserves source metadata when both paths are on the same filesystem; staging in `/tmp` (different mount) means we got a copy + new file with default umask perms. **Mitigated immediately** at Session 6a.3 with `chmod 600` + `chgrp staff` follow-up, but the ~30-second window was a real (small) exposure on this single-user, firewalled, Tailscale-only host. | **Operational lesson for future config edits:** when staging in `/tmp`, ALWAYS pair the `mv` with explicit `chmod 600` + `chgrp staff` immediately after, in the same script block, before running `openclaw gateway status`. **Better alternative when feasible:** stage in the same directory as the target (`~/.openclaw/openclaw.json.new`) so `mv` is rename-only and metadata is preserved. **Better still for small targeted edits:** use `openclaw config set ... --strict-json --merge` which the gateway-managed write path will mode-correct atomically. Apply this lesson at every subsequent file-replace edit (6.5.3, 6.5.4, 6.5.5, and any step 7 hardening edits). Owner: me, in next session's edit workflow. **F17 update 2026-04-25 (Session 6a.4): pattern proven twice (6.5.3, 6.5.4) on the in-`~/.openclaw/` staging path.** Workflow: stage with `jq` + redirect to `~/.openclaw/openclaw.json.new` (mv-rename within same directory preserves metadata atomically) → JSON-validate → diff for review → mv → `chmod 600 && chgrp staff` in same script block → 15s sleep → status check + log tail + Python deep-equal vs `.last-good`. Both edits landed clean: file mode 600 staff preserved across both, no exposure window. The `jq`-with-`--arg`-and-shell-variables pattern (see F14 v2) layers on top to defend against chat-layer rewriting of dotted basenames. This is now the standard config-edit workflow for 6.5.5 and any future `~/.openclaw/openclaw.json` edits where the data is too large or sensitive for `openclaw config set`. |
| F18 | Gateway canonicalises `openclaw.json` on load and may auto-add plugin entries for configured subsystems (added 2026-04-25 at Session 6a.3 step 6.5.2) | After the 6.5.2 file mv + restart, the gateway rewrote `~/.openclaw/openclaw.json` and saved our pre-rewrite version as `openclaw.json.bak`. Both are documented gateway behaviour, not faults; +53 bytes accounted for. **Implication:** future config edits that introduce a new top-level subsystem key may trigger a similar auto-add to `plugins.entries.*`. The `.bak` chain (`.bak`, `.bak.1`, `.bak.2`, `.last-good`) is gateway-maintained — our explicit timestamped backup from 6.5.1 was renamed to `.bak.2` during this housekeeping. | **Operational note for future edits:** after each file-replace + restart cycle, re-read live config and deep-equal-compare against our staged version using a Python `json.load` + `==` check (display-immune). Expect possible additions in `plugins.entries.*` for any new top-level subsystem; don't treat that as a fault. Don't manually maintain `.bak` files — gateway does it. As of end-of-6a.4: `plugins.entries` confirmed `['anthropic', 'browser']` only — `skills` and `hooks` are core subsystems, do NOT auto-register. Restart-trigger family stays `gateway.*`, `discovery.*`, `browser.*`. Empirical generalisation: subsystems whose runtime state is reachable through cache-invalidation (logger, skill snapshot, hook handler list) hot-reload; subsystems with bound auxiliary HTTP servers / sidecars (browser at 18791, discovery mDNS, gateway HTTP at 18789) restart-trigger. The earlier-emitted `[reload] config change detected; evaluating reload (X)` line is INFORMATIONAL ONLY — every reload (hot OR restart) emits it. Going forward, the v5 v3 classifier is: emit "evaluating reload" → check if "requires gateway restart" follows (within ~5ms) → if yes, restart; if no, hot-reload completes silently. Confirmed empirically: the 7.6 gateway-keys edit at 22:33:10 emitted "requires gateway restart" then SIGUSR1; the 7.8 logging edit at 23:26:02 emitted only "evaluating reload" with no follow-up restart line and no SIGUSR1. **Caveat noted at 6a.8:** schema field `logging.file` is read by the status surface (`openclaw gateway status`) but apparently NOT by the bundled file logger init — see F12 closure tail. Hot-reload is real (cache invalidation runs); the schema-vs-implementation gap is what makes the new log path stay empty. Subtle — the schema-confirmed override is being LOADED into config state (status surface proves it) but the file logger pino transport doesn't consult it on rebuild. **F18 v6 update 2026-04-27 (Session 6a.10 Phase 5): `agents.defaults.sandbox.*` is HOT-RELOAD same-PID, NOT restart-trigger, even with the new docker block.** Phase 5 config edit landed `mode: "off"` → `"all"` + 4 new sub-keys (scope, workspaceAccess, backend, docker). Plist-stdout gateway.log shows `[reload] config change detected; evaluating reload (agents.defaults.sandbox.mode, agents.defaults.sandbox.scope, agents.defaults.sandbox.workspaceAccess, agents.defaults.sandbox.backend, agents.defaults.sandbox.docker)` at 2026-04-27T10:57:47.134+01:00. **No follow-up WARN-line** `[gateway/reload] config change requires gateway restart (X)`. **No SIGUSR1, no `restarting`, no `loading configuration`, no new `ready` line.** PID 98076 unchanged before and after. live==.last-good: True after 30s settle. plugins.entries unchanged at `['anthropic', 'browser']` — no sandbox sidecar auto-registered. **Refines the F18 v3/v4 mental model:** the auxiliary-HTTP heuristic was necessary but not sufficient. The real classifier is whether the gateway must initialise the subsystem at its OWN boot time. Sandbox containers are spawned per-agent and lazily (gateway exec's `docker run` at agent invocation, not at gateway startup), so the docker-block config can hot-reload — gateway just rebuilds its sandbox-runner cache from new settings; the next `docker run` reads the updated image/network/readOnlyRoot. By contrast, browser/discovery/gateway-http have to bind ports at gateway boot, hence restart-trigger. **Reload-detection diff granularity also captured:** the gateway diff logic decomposes one level beneath `agents.defaults.sandbox` (5 sub-keys reported, including the docker block as a single object-replacement) but stops at object boundaries — it does not decompose docker.image / docker.network / docker.readOnlyRoot. Useful for predicting future reload-detection behaviour. **No `config hot reload applied` follow-up line for sandbox edit either** (matches the logging edit at 2026-04-26T23:26:02 — different subsystems report success differently; deep-equal vs `.last-good` is the authoritative signal, not the log line). **Updated mental model (F18 v6):** hot-reload same-PID family confirmed for `agents.*`, `agents.defaults.*` (including `agents.defaults.sandbox.*` with docker block), `skills.*`, `hooks.internal.entries.*`, `tools.deny`, `logging.*`. Restart-trigger family stays `gateway.*`, `discovery.*`, `browser.*`. Empirical generalisation: subsystems that are purely reference data the gateway reads on-demand at agent-spawn time (sandbox docker config) hot-reload like cache-invalidation subsystems; subsystems with bound auxiliary HTTP servers / sidecars that the gateway boots at startup (browser at 18791, discovery mDNS, gateway HTTP at 18789) restart-trigger. **6a.13 v7 substantive extension — `channels` family is split, NOT uniform.** Empirical at 9.3-prelude: `openclaw channels add --channel telegram --account pa` (FIRST telegram account ever; created top-level `channels` block from absent state) triggered RESTART. Log: `[reload] config change detected; evaluating reload (meta.lastTouchedAt, channels)` → `[gateway] signal SIGUSR1 received` → `[gateway] restart mode: full process restart (supervisor restart)` → PID 98076 → 80484 with new ready-line `(6 plugins: acpx, browser, device-pair, phone-control, talk-voice, telegram; 1.1s)` — `telegram` runtime plugin appeared in plugin list (extends F24). `openclaw channels remove --channel telegram --account pa --delete` (sub-key deletion; parent `channels.telegram.accounts` block already exists) triggered HOT-RELOAD same-PID 80484. Log: `[reload] config change detected; evaluating reload (meta.lastTouchedAt, channels.telegram.accounts)` → `[gateway/channels] restarting telegram channel` → `[reload] config hot reload applied (channels.telegram.accounts)`. **Boundary classification:** top-level `channels` block addition (creating from absent) = restart-trigger; sub-key add/remove `channels.<provider>.accounts.<id>` (parent established) = hot-reload. Sidecar restarts internally on hot-reload, not the gateway. **Practical effect at 6a.14:** with `channels.telegram.accounts` parent block now persistent (left in place by the surgical `--delete` rollback as `accounts: {}`), future `channels add` calls for Charlotte/Andreas/Sophie should hot-reload, not restart. Significantly faster per-bot pairing once cycle resumes. Marie (the bot whose `channels add` triggered the parent-block creation) is the only one that incurs the restart cost. **Updated v7 mental model:** Hot-reload same-PID family includes `agents.*` (with 6a.12 channel.* extension that was misframed — see F26 6a.13 update for the actual binding shape) / `agents.defaults.*` / `skills.*` / `hooks.internal.entries.*` / `tools.deny` / `logging.*` / `channels.<provider>.accounts.*` (sub-key add/remove). Restart-trigger family includes `gateway.*` / `discovery.*` / `browser.*` / `channels` (top-level, first-time block creation only). Classifier (gateway.err.log line `[reload] config change requires gateway restart (X)`) and success-line `[reload] config hot reload applied (X)` (gateway.log) work as predicted; both reliable signals. |

Doctor's heuristic ("dir under `agents/` without matching `agents.list[]` entry = orphan") is wrong for this case; doctor doesn't distinguish template vs agent. **Decision at 6.6:** leave `~/.openclaw/agents/main/` alone, document it as intentional infrastructure, ignore future doctor warnings about it. | **Operational note:** any future `openclaw doctor` run will repeat this orphan warning unless either (a) we add a `main` placeholder entry to `agents.list[]` (overkill — would need a fake workspace and model assignment for an agent that never runs), or (b) OpenClaw upstream improves doctor's heuristic. Doctor footer literally says `Run "openclaw doctor --fix" to apply changes.`. **Operational implication for S9 future automation:** auto-update validation flow can call `openclaw doctor --non-interactive --no-workspace-suggestions` safely as read-only health-check gate; suitable for launchd-bootstrapped cron-style invocation per F55 launchd path. | F21 | Auth-profiles.json content was rendered to chat during 6.6 investigation, exposing the Anthropic API key (added 2026-04-26 at Session 6a.5 step 6.6) | At step 6.6 doctor follow-up, the investigation block ran `head -80` on every non-empty file under `agents/main/`, which displayed the full plaintext value of the `anthropic:default` API key in chat output. The chat layer is a known exposure surface (training data, browser scrollback, IT screenshot tooling, message-store retention). Mitigated immediately by full key rotation: created new key in Anthropic console (named `openclaw-zone1-personal`), saved to 1Password, revoked the old key, then rotated the file value via `read -rs` (no echo) + `jq --arg` (display-immune). End state: old key revoked at Anthropic, new key in 1Password and `~/.openclaw/agents/main/agent/auth-profiles.json`, F22 lesson logged for future. **Note:** initial rotation produced an HTTP 401 from Anthropic when tested via `openclaw agent --agent pa --message ...` — likely paste-corruption mid-key (length and prefix passed but a character was wrong somewhere between positions 12 and 100). Re-rotated with stricter paste verification (full-key SHA-256 prefix computed at paste-time, round-trip verified post-write). Live test of the second rotation deferred to next session per context budget. | **Operational lesson moving forward:** never `cat`, `head`, or otherwise echo files known to contain secrets (`auth-profiles.json`, anything under `~/.openclaw/credentials/`, `.env`, OAuth tokens, gateway auth token). When inspection is needed, pipe through `jq 'del(.profiles[].key)'` or similar to strip secrets before output. For any "show me what's in this file" command on sensitive paths, use `jq` with explicit `del()` for known-sensitive keys, or pre-filter to declared-safe fields only (`type`, `provider`, `version`, `length` of the secret). For unknown sensitive paths, prefer `ls -la` + size + SHA-256 over content display. **Standard rotation hygiene:** create new → save to 1Password → revoke old (in that order); never both at once; never delete the only copy of a credential without confirming the replacement works. **Verification pattern for key writes:** compute SHA-256 prefix at paste-time, write via `jq --arg`, read back from disk and re-compute SHA-256 — round-trip match confirms the bytes on disk equal the bytes pasted. Length and prefix-only checks are insufficient (saw 6a.5 401 case where 108-char prefix-`sk-ant-api03` key was still corrupt mid-string). Owner: me, in every future session that touches credentials. **CLOSED 2026-04-26 at Session 6a.6 step 7.** Live API round-trip validated end-to-end. Diagnostic at 6a.6 first action: `openclaw agent --agent pa --message "Reply with the single word: ROTATED" --json --timeout 60` — initially failed with HTTP 401 again, profile fingerprint `sha256:154a23a3efe6`. **Root cause: stale per-agent materialised auth-profiles copy.** Display-immune SHA inspection of both files: `agents/main/agent/auth-profiles.json` had the rotated key (prefix `fb0ec87d4394`, len 108, mode 600 staff — matched 6a.5 reference) but `agents/pa/agent/auth-profiles.json` had a DIFFERENT prefix (`35fc0f99a089`, len 108, mode 600 staff) — the OLD revoked key. PA's file had been materialised at 6a.5 doctor invocation BEFORE the 6a.5 rotation; the rotation only edited `main/`, leaving PA's stale copy intact. Auth-profiles inheritance is **materialise-once**, not live: once `agents/<id>/agent/auth-profiles.json` exists, the runner reads it directly without re-checking `main/`. Fix applied: `rm ~/.openclaw/agents/pa/agent/auth-profiles.json` → re-ran agent CLI → log line `[agents/auth-profiles] inherited auth-profiles from main agent` confirmed re-materialisation → response 200, `payloads[0].text` = real model output, real billing event (input=4, output=257, cacheRead=9113, cacheWrite=11098, total=10528 tokens), `executionTrace.attempts[0].result: success`, `stopReason: stop`. Cooldown didn't apply because re-materialisation produced fresh fingerprint. Post-fix SHA verification: both `main/` and `pa/` files match `fb0ec87d4394` len 108 mode 600 staff. Anthropic console confirmed: only one active key (the rotated one); old key disabled and removed. Estimated $0.05 cost on the test run, billed correctly to the new key. **New operational lesson — credential rotation discipline:** rotating in `agents/main/agent/auth-profiles.json` only covers agents that have NOT yet materialised their own per-agent copy. Any agent that has materialised before rotation will silently keep using the old (revoked) key. **Rule for every future auth-profile rotation:** edit `main/`, then either (a) `rm ~/.openclaw/agents/*/agent/auth-profiles.json` for all materialised per-agent copies and let them re-inherit lazily on next run, or (b) `cp main/agent/auth-profiles.json` → each materialised per-agent path + `chmod 600 && chgrp staff` in same script block. As of 6a.6 only `pa` had materialised; the other 8 agents will inherit fresh from rotated `main/` on their first invocation. Pattern applies equally to gateway-token rotations and any future provider-key changes. See F23 for downstream issue uncovered during this work (BOOTSTRAP.md truncation). |
| F22 | zsh history scrubbing: `history -d` is bash syntax, doesn't work in zsh (added 2026-04-26 at Session 6a.5 step 6.6) | At the end of the auth-key rotation in 6a.5, the cleanup tail of the apply command included `history -d $(history | tail -3 | head -1 | awk '{print $1}')` to scrub the read-NEW_KEY line. Output showed the three commands STILL in history — zsh ignored the `-d` flag (zsh's `history` builtin doesn't take `-d`; it uses `fc -p` / `print -s` for adding-but-not-deleting, and history file edits go through `~/.zsh_history` directly). **Net impact:** the `read -rs 'NEW_KEY?...'` lines remain in `~/.zsh_history`, but they only contain the prompt string, not the key value (the value went into the `NEW_KEY` shell variable, never into the command line — that's the entire point of `read -rs`). So the history file is benign. Worth knowing for future rotation/secret commands. | **Operational note:** when scrubbing zsh history is needed for real (e.g. if a command line itself contained a secret), use `fc -W` to write current history to file, then edit `~/.zsh_history` directly with `sed -i '' '/pattern/d' ~/.zsh_history` (BSD sed on macOS). Or run sensitive commands in a subshell with `unset HISTFILE; HISTFILE=/dev/null` set BEFORE the read, persisting only inside the subshell. For the auth-rotation pattern specifically, current discipline is sufficient: keys never leave the `NEW_KEY` shell variable; `unset NEW_KEY` clears memory; `~/.zsh_history` only sees the `read -rs` prompt strings. Owner: me, apply correct zsh syntax in any future credential-handling commands. |

New pending request `3353be2e-8e33-4593-95da-156af6e892d5` joins the regen cycle, will age out before step 9. **6a.12 substantive update 2026-04-27 — Path A canonical-docs investigation complete; scope decision committed.** Investigation per F26 closure path. Architecture-grep discipline (sustained from 6a.10) ran first: v5 spec is silent on operator-device pairing scopes — no `operator.*` references anywhere; "scope" mentions are about Gmail OAuth (line 49), sandbox `scope: "agent"` (line 846), payment authorisation (line 864), CoS access reviews (line 328). No spec override or refinement on bot pairing scope. Implementation detail not covered in v5 spec; canonical OpenClaw docs are the source of truth. **Path A — canonical docs:** initial fetch attempt on `docs.openclaw.ai/devices/scopes` returned 404 (URL was a guess based on F11/F15/F16 docs.openclaw.ai path conventions, not a confirmed canonical path). Fell to web-search across openclaw.ai docs + github.com/openclaw/openclaw source repo + known-recent issues. Evidence stack converged: (a) **bootstrap allowlist of 4 scopes documented for paired operator devices**: `operator.approvals, operator.read, operator.talk.secrets, operator.write` — sourced from the channels/pairing docs (third-party-mirror surfaced via search at openclaw-docs.beaverslab.xyz/en/channels/pairing; could not directly fetch the canonical docs.openclaw.ai/channels/pairing due to web-fetch permissions wall on URLs not surfaced in prior search results — minor source-confidence caveat noted). (b) **canonical pairing.md from github.com/openclaw/openclaw/blob/main/docs/gateway/pairing.md** clarifies critical role taxonomy: `node.pair.*` is a SEPARATE pairing flow used only for capability-host nodes (camera/canvas/screen/system.run); WS device pairing during the `connect` handshake is what gates the operator-role connection bots use. Telegram bots are operator role per `protocol.md` ("operator = control plane client (CLI/UI/automation). node = capability host."). (c) **Independent corroboration on operator.read insufficiency: GitHub issue #70687** (filed 4 days ago against 2026.4.21, one patch off our 2026.4.22 build) reports identical symptom class to F26 — `telegram/native-approvals connect error: scope upgrade pending approval`, `failed to start native approval handler` — when device scopes were reset to only `operator.read`. The fix per the issue: restore the additional scopes that spawn-subagent + native-approvals operations need. Issue doesn't enumerate the exact set, but its symptom matches the bootstrap allowlist's coverage. **Per-scope rationale committed:** `operator.read` (high confidence — necessary baseline; F26 6a.10 empirical confirmed insufficient alone), `operator.write` (high confidence — bots send messages back, spawn subagents per issue #70687), `operator.approvals` (high confidence — `telegram/native-approvals` handler explicitly fails without per issue #70687), `operator.talk.secrets` (medium confidence — defensible inclusion: in documented bootstrap profile, scope-domain narrowly defined as secrets-in-conversation-context, failure mode if missing is obscure mid-flow on secret-shaped payloads, failure mode if present-but-unused is zero). Excluded scopes: `operator.pairing` (pairing-management; bots don't pair other devices), `operator.admin` (cross-device admin; bots don't manage other devices). **Decision committed for 4 bot devices (Marie/Charlotte/Andreas/Sophie):** scope set `operator.read + operator.write + operator.approvals + operator.talk.secrets` — the documented bootstrap-profile baseline. **Decision committed for CLI device (currently at `operator.read`):** stay at `operator.read` per F26 closure-doc lean. Reject any pending scope-upgrade request as it ages out and regens; embedded fallback covers non-gateway-required CLI ops (verified empirically across 6a.6/6a.10/6a.11 sessions). Approval is one-way per F26 lock-in concern; over-broad CLI scope is durable risk for marginal benefit. Bot devices are the action-taking devices in this architecture; CLI stays low-privilege querier. **F26 partial closure:** scope decision committed (this update). **Full closure:** at step 9.3 first bot device pairing + agent invocation succeeding via gateway path (empirical confirmation that the 4-scope set is correct). Failure mode if scope decision wrong: WebSocket 1008 close on bot pairing handshake — visible immediately, rotate to wider/narrower scope and re-pair (~2 min recovery). Blast radius bounded: single-user trust boundary per D7 + threat model in F4 closure. Path B (empirical scope-widening) not invoked — Path A delivered with sufficient confidence to commit. **Owner:** me, applies at 9.3 via `openclaw devices pair --role operator --scope operator.read --scope operator.write --scope operator.approvals --scope operator.talk.secrets` (CLI flag form per `docs.openclaw.ai/cli/devices` rotate syntax — verify `pair` subcommand accepts the same `--scope` repeats at 9.3 prep). **6a.13 substantive corrections — bot pairing flow + scope-at-approve + tokenFile semantics. F26 stays partial-closure (scope decision committed at 6a.12); empirical closure remains pending at 6a.14.** Three structural findings at 9.3-prelude that invalidate parts of the 6a.12 closure-doc plan: **(1) `openclaw devices pair` does NOT exist.** Devices subcommand surface is `approve / clear / help / list / reject / remove / revoke / rotate`. The 6a.12 closure doc's planned form `openclaw devices pair --role operator --scope ... --scope ...` is not a real CLI surface. **Actual bot-bring-up flow:** `openclaw channels add --channel telegram --account <id> --bot-token|--token-file ... --name <display>` writes to live config; gateway's phone-control runtime plugin sees the new account, brings up Bot API session, the bot's WS-handshake to gateway generates a pending device-pair request that appears in `openclaw devices list`; CLI runs `openclaw devices approve <requestId>` to grant. **(2) `devices approve` does NOT take `--scope`.** Flag set is `--help, --json, --latest, --password, --timeout, --token, --url`. Scope is determined by the REQUESTING device at handshake time, not at approve time. So the 6a.12 plan's scope-set is enforced by what the bot-side handshake asks for, not by CLI flags. Empirically: at 6a.13 the channel sidecar for Marie produced no pending request because the bot couldn't authenticate to Telegram (see F37) — the requested-scope set is therefore unobserved at 6a.13. At 6a.14 with Marie's bot bringing up cleanly, the pending request will surface; we observe its requested scope, validate it matches the F26 4-scope decision, and approve. If the request asks wider, narrow via reject + reconfigure (probably not feasible — channel sidecar's requested scope is hard-coded by the plugin, not configurable). If narrower, approve as-is and note the empirical scope reduction. **(3) Channel binding canonical shape is two top-level config blocks**, NOT `agents.list[].channel.*` per the 6a.12 handoff doc reframing — the handoff misinferred from observing empty agents.list rows. Architecture spec §2.5 lines 1152-1183 confirm: top-level `channels: { telegram: { accounts: { <id>: {botToken, dmPolicy, ...} } } }` for provider config + top-level `bindings: [{type, agentId, comment, match: {channel, accountId, peer}}]` for routing. Schema at `.properties.bindings` confirms exactly. Live config has 14 top-level keys including `channels` and `auth` etc., distinct from `agents`. **(4) `agents bind` is the canonical bindings management surface** (NOT direct jq edit on the bindings array). Flags: `--agent <id> --bind <channel[:accountId]>`, repeatable. Concrete Marie call: `openclaw agents bind --agent pa --bind telegram:pa`. Recovery surfaces are `agents unbind --agent <id> --bind <channel[:accountId]>` (precise) or `--all` (nuclear). **(5) CLI's pending scope-upgrade request reject path validated empirically.** At 6a.13, `openclaw devices reject d83dc921-…` removed the request cleanly; CLI stayed at `operator.read` paired status. New regen request appeared on next gateway-touching invocation (`35c0025e-…`, then `6fa1dc20-…`); regen treadmill is normal noise. **Operational rule:** at 6a.14 when `openclaw devices list` shows pending requests, distinguish bot-pending from CLI-regen by deviceId prefix — CLI is `90f13707b…`, bots will have different prefixes. **NEVER use `devices approve --latest` once bots are pending** — `--latest` would target whichever pending appeared most recently, which may be CLI regen. Approve by full requestId only. **Reformulated 9.3 plan for 6a.14:** 9.3a (read-only sanity, capture new agents.list SHA which shifted again post-6a.13 channels-add rollback to `accounts: {}`) → 9.3b-pre (reject latest CLI pending if present) → 9.3b (channels add × 4 with durable token-files per F37 — Charlotte/Andreas/Sophie should hot-reload now that parent `channels.telegram.accounts` block exists per F18 v7) → 9.3c (`agents bind` × 4) → 9.3d (`devices approve` × 4 by full requestId) → 9.3e (F26 empirical closure on Marie's first agent invocation via gateway path). **6a.14 substantive update — 9.3b-pre approach empirically rejected; F40 captures.** At 6a.14: `devices reject 28f1d090-…` failed with WS-1008 close pattern; --token bypass via `auth.token` failed (field returns JSON `null`, GT length 4, GT SHA-12 `74234e98afe7` is canonical SHA of literal `"null"`). 9.3b-pre rejected as sub-unit per F26 6a.10 noise-vs-blockage rule (CLI elevated-scope pending row blocks CLI self-reject but does NOT block bot-pairing). 9.3 plan revised to 4 sub-units for 6a.15: 9.3b channels add × 4 → 9.3c agents bind × 4 → 9.3d devices approve × 4 → 9.3e F26 empirical closure. **6a.15 SUBSTANTIVE UPDATE — F26 architectural closure complete; F26 scope decision validated empirically; F26 empirical closure (full agent-routing) deferred to 6b. Several structural corrections to canonical bot-pairing flow.** **(1) The canonical bot-pairing flow is per-user via `dmPolicy: "pairing"` + `openclaw pairing approve` cycle, NOT the OpenClaw `devices` table — that table is for human-controlling-OpenClaw devices (phone, laptop CLI), not for bot-token-authenticated Telegram peer authorisation.** Empirical evidence at 6a.15: when Marie's bot was fully operational (channels-added, dmPolicy=pairing, agents-bound, provider running connected), Peter's Telegram client auto-sent `/start` on first chat-open. Bot replied with pairing-handshake message (`OpenClaw: access not configured. Your Telegram user id: 253509519. Pairing code: 8RZZ3RSV. Ask the bot owner to approve with: openclaw pairing approve telegram 8RZZ3RSV`). PA agent was NOT invoked — pairing layer intercepted the message before agent dispatch. CLI runs `openclaw pairing approve --channel telegram --account <accountId> [--notify] <code>` to whitelist that Telegram user as authorised peer. Approval persists durably at `~/.openclaw/credentials/telegram-<accountId>-allowFrom.json` shape `{"version": 1, "allowFrom": ["<telegram_user_id_as_string>"]}`. Pairing-codes table at `~/.openclaw/credentials/telegram-pairing.json` shape `{"version": 1, "requests": [...]}` — code consumed on approval (drained to empty). **`devices approve` is for OpenClaw control-plane devices (CLI, mobile-app companion); `pairing approve` is for per-bot per-user Telegram peer authorisation. They are orthogonal subsystems.** F26 6a.13 update item (1) characterisation of "channel sidecar handshake → CLI devices approve <requestId>" was empirically wrong; the actual flow has zero `devices` table interaction for bot-channel-binding-pairing. **(2) `pairing` subcommand surface is `approve, list, help`. There is NO `revoke` subcommand.** Once a peer is pairing-approved, removal requires either direct edit of the `telegram-<accountId>-allowFrom.json` file OR `channels remove --account <id> --delete` cycle (which would also invalidate bot token reference). **(3) Pairing approvals leave NO audit trail in `gateway.log` or `gateway.err.log`** — neither the pairing-handshake DM (incoming `/start` + pairing-code reply) nor the approval action emit log entries to either file. Gateway-internal state-change only. Sub-fact for step 15 cron/healthcheck design: pairing-flow auditing requires watching `~/.openclaw/credentials/` for file changes, not log-tailing. **(4) `pairing approve --notify` failed with `telegram token not configured`** — related-to-but-not-blocking F40 (separate code path that doesn't traverse the same auth chain as the channel provider). The approval itself landed cleanly without notify; the post-approval Telegram DM to the user just didn't fire. Defer investigation to 6b or step 15. **(5) F26 scope decision empirically VALIDATED** — Marie's bot brought up `running, connected, mode:polling, token:config`, Telegram getMe identity confirmed (`@marie_pf_bot`), pairing-handshake worked end-to-end. The bot did NOT need to be paired in OpenClaw `devices` table to be operational. Whatever scope the channel provider runs at internally is sufficient for pairing-handshake + future agent-dispatch. The 6a.12 4-scope-set decision (`operator.read + operator.write + operator.approvals + operator.talk.secrets`) was committed for OpenClaw control-plane devices, but per (1) above, bots don't go through that path; F26 scope decision is now operationally moot for bot devices and remains correct for any future control-plane device pairings. **F26 architectural closure: COMPLETE.** All 4 bots (Marie/Charlotte/Andreas/Sophie) channel-added + dmPolicy=pairing + agents-bound + providers running connected. Marie pairing-approved (Peter durably whitelisted). **F26 empirical closure (full agent-routing end-to-end via gateway path with workspace-authored agent personas): DEFERRED to 6b.** Per spec step 31, no DM to any of the 4 bots until proper PA workspace authoring complete. Charlotte/Andreas/Sophie pairing approvals batch at 6b alongside their first-DM-from-Peter cycles. F26 row stays open as administrative formality through 6b PA bootstrap session. **6a.23 close sub-correction:** F26 empirical closure path moved from 6b to **6a.27 pre-6b validation gate session per S8 sub-item (e)(i)**. Rationale: the empirical concern is wire-validity (channel→gateway→agent path works end-to-end), which does not require PA workspace authoring. A graceful "I don't have workspace files yet per scaffolding template" response from any of the 4 bots passes the F26 wire test. This decouples F26 closure from spec step 31 PA bootstrap message protocol (which governs avoiding real-task-as-first-message, not wire validation). Charlotte/Andreas/Sophie pairing approvals batch at 6a.27 if they happen during gate session, else at 6b alongside their first-DM-from-Peter cycles. **6a.32 (A-1) empirical:** 4 bots enabled/configured/running/connected (polling-live = F2 liveness); zero pairing/scope fields; `channels status` shows no paired device sessions. Device-pairing scope upgrade NOT done. F26 stays OPEN, discharge at 6b (pairing approvals + scope decision at PA operational). |
| F27 | Docker socket access blocker for sandbox build (added 2026-04-27 at Session 6a.8 step 7.9 pre-flight) | OpenClaw v5 spec §4.1 requires `agents.defaults.sandbox.backend = "docker"` with `openclaw-sandbox:bookworm-slim` image. Pre-flight investigation at 6a.8 step 7.9 reveals: `docker --version` works (29.4.0 installed), but `docker info` fails with `permission denied while trying to connect to the docker API at unix:///var/run/docker.sock` from the `openclaw` user. **Diagnosis:** `/var/run/docker.sock` is a SYMLINK to `/Users/pfedchenkov/.docker/run/docker.sock` (created by Docker Desktop install at 11:02 24-Apr 2026, owned root:daemon). The actual socket is owned by `pfedchenkov:staff` mode `srwxr-xr-x` — group `staff` (which includes `openclaw` per `id openclaw`) has read+execute but NOT write on the socket. `docker info`'s Server-side request requires write to the socket, hence the denial. **Architectural concern beyond the surface symptom:** Docker Desktop is running as user `pfedchenkov` (confirmed via ps: `com.docker.virtualization` instance with disk `/Users/pfedchenkov/Library/Containers/com.docker.docker/Data/vms/0/data/Docker.raw`, virtiofs mounts). Even if `openclaw` is granted write permission on the socket, `openclaw`-spawned containers would run inside `pfedchenkov`'s VM, sharing pfedchenkov's container namespace. This violates the D8 user-isolation logic — the entire reason `openclaw` exists as a separate user is to keep agent runtime isolated from Peter's primary user. A container escape inside a Docker-Desktop-managed VM owned by `pfedchenkov` lands in `pfedchenkov`'s VM, not in a contained `openclaw`-owned environment. **No alternative runtime currently installed:** Colima, OrbStack, Lima, Podman, nerdctl all absent (`which` returns not-found for each). | **Decision required at start of Session 6a.9.** Three options: **(1) chmod the existing socket to grant openclaw write** — cheap fix, full architectural compromise, NOT recommended (defeats D8 isolation). **(2) Install Colima as openclaw-owned runtime** — recommended path. Colima runs a separate VM under the invoking user (`/Users/openclaw/.colima/...`), separate socket at `~/.colima/default/docker.sock` owned by openclaw, separate container namespace. Vanilla `dockerd` inside, predictable for OpenClaw's `sandbox-setup.sh` script. ARM-native via `vm-type vz` on Apple Silicon. Brew-installable. Cost: ~10-15 min install, ~60-90 min total session for full 7.9 (including sandbox-setup.sh script run, docker build, agents.defaults.sandbox config edit, sandbox-mode agent test). **(3) Install OrbStack as openclaw-owned runtime** — faster than Colima/Docker Desktop but commercial software (license model may apply to Peter's use), and OrbStack's diverged-from-vanilla architecture occasionally surprises build scripts. Less predictable than Colima for an OpenClaw build script. **My recommendation at end of 6a.8: (2) Colima.** Confirmed by Peter end of 6a.8. **Owner:** me at 6a.9. Open at 6a.9 with: install Colima as `pfedchenkov` (or via brew under openclaw if openclaw has brew), `colima start --arch aarch64 --vm-type vz --cpu 4 --memory 8 --disk 60`, set docker context, then proceed to clone openclaw repo as `pfedchenkov` to `~/src/openclaw` (no GitHub creds on `openclaw` user), run sandbox-setup.sh script, edit `agents.defaults.sandbox` config, test sandbox-mode agent run. **CLOSED 2026-04-27 at Session 6a.9 end of Phase 4 step 3.** F27 architectural concern fully resolved end-to-end. Phase sequence executed at 6a.9: **Phase 1** F27 recommendation re-confirmed with Peter (Colima vs chmod-sock vs OrbStack); Colima confirmed. **Phase 2a** `brew install colima` as `pfedchenkov` — colima 0.10.1, lima 2.1.1 dep, binary at `/opt/homebrew/bin/colima`. Switched to `openclaw` via `sudo -i -u openclaw`. `colima start --cpu 6 --memory 8 --disk 60 --vm-type vz --arch aarch64` — VM at `/Users/openclaw/.colima/default/`, socket at `~/.colima/default/docker.sock` mode `0600 openclaw:staff` (tighter than Docker Desktop's `0755` socket — architectural concern about cross-user namespace sharing fully addressed). Docker context `colima` set current; Docker Desktop's `default` context registered but not current. Server = vanilla dockerd 29.2.1 in Ubuntu 24.04.4 LTS VM, overlayfs storage, runc default runtime. ~58s end-to-end (download phase 55s for ~250MB Lima base, VM boot + dockerd start ~3s on M4 + vz framework). **Phase 2b** Docker Desktop graceful quit via `osascript -e 'quit app "Docker Desktop"'` as `pfedchenkov` — frees the 6GB Desktop VM allocation back to macOS; ~10 docker processes shut down cleanly (UI app, backend, buildkit, GPU helper, network helper, virtualization VM at PID 37708 with `--cpus 6 --memoryMiB 6144`). Colima sanity check post-quit confirmed Desktop quit didn't perturb openclaw's VM. Privileged helper `com.docker.vmnetd` and Login Items entry remain — see F29 for the deferred full-retirement scope. **Phase 3** `git clone https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw.git` as `openclaw` to `/Users/openclaw/src/openclaw/` via HTTPS (deviation from handoff plan — openclaw clone preferred over pfedchenkov for single-user-ownership of the build pipeline, surfaced and approved). 595MB pull, 482657 objects, HEAD at `edbab0e2db` (4 patch versions ahead of running daemon at 4.22 commit `00bd2cf` — gateway upgrade is a separate question, out of scope for 7.9). Build script (10 lines) + Dockerfile (24 lines) + docker-build.sh helper reviewed; image is generic Debian-slim + 7 apt packages, daemon-version-agnostic, building from HEAD without `git checkout 00bd2cf` was the right call. **Phase 4 step 1 pre-flight failure** — `BuildKit is enabled but the buildx component is missing or broken`. Investigation read-only first per 6a.8 lesson. Inventory confirmed: no `~openclaw/.docker/cli-plugins/`, no buildx anywhere on plugin search path, `/usr/local/bin/docker 29.4.0` (Docker Desktop's CLI binary) is what `openclaw` invokes. Three options surfaced; option (A) `brew install docker-buildx` + per-user symlink chosen as MVP fix (rejected option (B) brew docker CLI replacement as logged in F30, rejected option (C) BuildKit disable because Dockerfile requires `# syntax=docker/dockerfile:1.7` + cache mounts). Fix: `brew install docker-buildx` as `pfedchenkov` (binary v0.33.0 at `/opt/homebrew/opt/docker-buildx/bin/docker-buildx`, brew-managed symlink at `/opt/homebrew/lib/docker/cli-plugins/docker-buildx`); as `openclaw` `mkdir -p ~/.docker/cli-plugins && ln -sf /opt/homebrew/lib/docker/cli-plugins/docker-buildx ~/.docker/cli-plugins/docker-buildx`. `docker buildx version` resolves cleanly under openclaw at v0.33.0. **Phase 4 step 2 build successful** — `bash scripts/sandbox-setup.sh` ran clean in ~21s wall time. BuildKit instance `colima`, base `debian:bookworm-slim@sha256:4724b8cc...` matched Dockerfile digest pin, 47 packages installed (7 declared + 40 deps), 30.1MB downloaded, image manifest list `sha256:e59beddc206d86329e05a8f83be5b2ac20765300d106dab9187f6e3659ae03ab`, 335MB on-disk / 76.3MB content. **Phase 4 step 3 smoke test** under `--read-only --network none` (mirrors §4.1 sandbox runtime flags): `uid=1000(sandbox)` non-privileged user enforced, `aarch64` ARM-native (not Rosetta-emulated), all 4 runtime tools functional inside the read-only no-network container (ripgrep 13.0.0, jq-1.6, Python 3.11.2, git 2.39.5). **Net state at 6a.9 close:** openclaw owns its VM, its docker socket, its container namespace, its sandbox image. F27's "isolation violation" concern fully neutralised — a container escape lands in openclaw's owned VM, not pfedchenkov's. Day 1 build pipeline working end-to-end; persistence across reboot deferred (F28); Docker Desktop full uninstall + CLI brew migration deferred (F29 + F30); none of these block step 7.9 Phase 5+6 (config edit + agent verify) which carries cleanly into Session 6a.10. **Owner closes:** me at 6a.9. F15 sandbox build sub-concern progressed but stays open for the remaining config edit + agent verify in 6a.10. |
| F28 | Colima auto-start across reboot deferred — must NOT use `brew services start colima` (added 2026-04-27 at Session 6a.9 Phase 2a step 1) | After `brew install colima` as `pfedchenkov`, brew Caveats suggested `brew services start colima` for persistence. **Deliberately NOT used.** `brew services start colima` would launchd-register Colima under the user that ran the command (`pfedchenkov`) — recreating the F27 problem in reverse: Colima VM, socket, and container namespace owned by `pfedchenkov`, useless to `openclaw`. The architecturally-correct persistence answer is a launchd plist under `~openclaw/Library/LaunchAgents/`, modelled on the gateway's `ai.openclaw.gateway.plist`, that runs `colima start` as `openclaw` at openclaw's first login. Day 1 state at 6a.9: `colima start` ran manually as `openclaw` with VM at `/Users/openclaw/.colima/default/`, socket at `~/.colima/default/docker.sock`. The lima-managed VM persists across openclaw shell sessions / SSH disconnects within the same login session, but does NOT survive a Mac Mini reboot until launchd persistence is added. Per D11, full reboots already require manual user login at the Mini for FileVault, so the gateway already has a manual-login dependency post-reboot — Colima will share that dependency, not introduce a new one. Net effect: today's manual `colima start` is sufficient for 7.9 and for normal operation as long as the Mini stays up. | **Phase 0 cleanup item, not blocking 7.9 or step 7 closure.** Plan when revisiting: write `~openclaw/Library/LaunchAgents/ai.openclaw.colima.plist` modelled on the gateway plist (`StandardOutPath`/`StandardErrorPath` to `~/.openclaw/logs/colima.log` + `colima.err.log`; `Program` `/opt/homebrew/bin/colima`; `ProgramArguments` `[colima, start, --cpu, 6, --memory, 8, --disk, 60, --vm-type, vz, --arch, aarch64]`; `RunAtLoad: true`; `KeepAlive: false` because `colima start` exits cleanly after the VM is up; `EnvironmentVariables` with `PATH=/opt/homebrew/bin:/usr/bin:/bin:/usr/sbin:/sbin` so the binary resolves). `launchctl bootstrap` it as openclaw. **Load-order concern:** the gateway plist must wait for Colima's socket before the gateway daemon connects to docker — either via a `WaitForSocket` mechanism (if launchd supports it for the colima socket path), or a small wrapper script in the gateway plist that polls `~/.colima/default/docker.sock` for ~30s before exec'ing `node …/dist/index.js gateway`. Test post-implementation by full Mini reboot + manual openclaw login + verify (a) colima auto-starts, (b) gateway connects to docker context without intervention, (c) sandbox-mode agent run succeeds. **Owner:** me, on a future session — natural batch is Phase 0 step 7 closure cleanup or post-step-8, not the 7.9 critical path. **Reference:** brew install output 6a.9 Phase 2a step 1 included Caveat `To start colima now and restart at login: brew services start colima` — the exact path this flag exists to forbid. |

Idle <50MB when Desktop isn't actively talking to it. **(3) `/Applications/Docker.app/`** — ~2GB on disk, includes the CLI binary at `/Applications/Docker.app/Contents/Resources/bin/docker` which `/usr/local/bin/docker` symlinks to (CLI removal coupled with this — see F30). **(4) `~/Library/Containers/com.docker.docker/`** under pfedchenkov — VM disk image (~6GB) plus app group containers, settings, log dirs. Recoverable disk space. **(5) `~/.docker/`** under pfedchenkov — desktop-specific contexts, settings, ephemeral CLI plugins. **(6) `/usr/local/bin/docker`** symlink itself — handle at F30 migration time. **Net effect of partial state at 6a.9 close:** Desktop is quit and won't run unless someone logs into pfedchenkov's GUI session (which isn't part of normal headless-via-SSH operation). The 6GB VM allocation isn't being held while Desktop isn't running. Auto-restart only triggers on next pfedchenkov GUI login. Acceptable for daily operation; should still be cleaned up to remove the auto-restart vector and reclaim ~8GB on disk. | **Future cleanup pass — not blocking step 7 closure or downstream work.** Plan: (a) Screen Share or local pfedchenkov session, System Settings → Login Items & Extensions → toggle Docker off. (b) `sudo launchctl bootout system /Library/LaunchDaemons/com.docker.vmnetd.plist 2>/dev/null; sudo rm -f /Library/LaunchDaemons/com.docker.* /Library/PrivilegedHelperTools/com.docker.vmnetd`. (c) `rm -rf /Applications/Docker.app ~/Library/Containers/com.docker.docker ~/Library/Group\ Containers/group.com.docker* ~/Library/Application\ Support/Docker\ Desktop ~/Library/Caches/com.docker.docker ~/Library/Logs/Docker\ Desktop ~/.docker` (paths inferred from standard Desktop install layout — verify each with `ls -la` before bulk delete). (d) Coordinate `/usr/local/bin/docker` migration with F30 (remove Desktop's symlinked CLI, install brew docker as the replacement, ensure openclaw's PATH still resolves docker). (e) Test post-cleanup by full Mini reboot + verify Colima starts manually under openclaw, gateway connects to colima docker context, sandbox-mode agent run succeeds. Should be unchanged from current Phase 4 state. **Owner:** me + Peter (Screen Share for step a) on a future session — natural batch with F30 docker CLI migration and possibly with F28's launchd plist authoring. Not on the 7.9 critical path. |
| F30 | `/usr/local/bin/docker` is Docker Desktop's CLI binary, not brew's — replace with `brew install docker` for cleaner long-term state (added 2026-04-27 at Session 6a.9 Phase 4 step 1) | At 6a.9 Phase 4 step 1, the buildx-missing pre-flight investigation confirmed `which docker` returns `/usr/local/bin/docker` — Docker Desktop's CLI binary (Desktop installs the CLI at this path during first-run privileged install, symlinked to `/Applications/Docker.app/Contents/Resources/bin/docker`). Even though Desktop itself is now quit and openclaw uses the Colima docker context, the CLI binary openclaw is invoking still belongs to Docker Desktop. When Desktop is fully retired (F29), removing `/Applications/Docker.app` will leave `/usr/local/bin/docker` as a broken symlink, and the broken docker CLI breaks everything that depends on it (gateway sandbox spawn, manual `docker` invocations, build/run cycles). Cleaner long-term state: `brew install docker` (the CLI-only formula, not Desktop) installs a vendor-neutral CLI at `/opt/homebrew/bin/docker` that talks to whichever socket the active context points at (Colima in our case). Brew docker also installs CLI plugins under `/opt/homebrew/etc/docker/cli-plugins/` which is on the docker CLI's search path by default — eliminates the per-user symlink we set up at 6a.9 Phase 4 step 1 fix (the openclaw → `/opt/homebrew/lib/docker/cli-plugins/docker-buildx` symlink) once we confirm brew docker finds buildx via the etc path. | **Future migration item, batched with F29.** Plan: (1) `brew install docker` as pfedchenkov — installs CLI to `/opt/homebrew/bin/docker`, brew CLI plugin search path picks up `/opt/homebrew/etc/docker/cli-plugins/`. (2) Verify under openclaw: `which docker` should resolve via PATH order to `/opt/homebrew/bin/docker` if `/opt/homebrew/bin` precedes `/usr/local/bin` in openclaw's PATH (per F9 closure: `~openclaw/.zshenv` puts homebrew first via `path_helper`). If `/usr/local/bin/docker` still wins on PATH, that's because Desktop's PATH injection or `path_helper`'s ordering hasn't updated; fix by removing `/usr/local/bin/docker` (F29 step c removes `/Applications/Docker.app` which removes the symlink target; the broken symlink itself can be `rm`-ed). (3) Verify `docker buildx version` still resolves under openclaw — brew docker's plugin search path includes `/opt/homebrew/etc/docker/cli-plugins/` and `/opt/homebrew/lib/docker/cli-plugins/`, so the existing `/opt/homebrew/lib/docker/cli-plugins/docker-buildx` symlink chain (brew-managed) keeps working. (5) Test sandbox-mode agent run end-to-end. **Owner:** me on a future session — natural batch with F29 cleanup pass. Not on the 7.9 critical path. |
| F31 | Sandbox containers are persistent (`sleep infinity`, AutoRemove false), not ephemeral — accumulate over time without explicit cleanup (added 2026-04-27 at Session 6a.10 Phase 6) | Phase 6 docker inspect on sandbox container `9a685955b735` (named `openclaw-sbx-agent-pa-9606a5de`) revealed `Cmd: ["sleep", "infinity"]`, `AutoRemove: false`. The gateway pattern is: spawn a long-lived sandbox container per agent at first agent invocation, then run each subsequent agent turn via `docker exec` against the same container. Faster than spawn-and-destroy per call, but means stopped containers will accumulate over time as agents come, go, and roll over sessions. After Phase 6 the container was still running (`Up 9 seconds` in step-4 readout, hours later it would still be there if the agent stays warm). Naming pattern `openclaw-sbx-agent-<agentId>-<8-char-hex>` is gateway-managed; the hex appears to be a session/instance suffix. **Schema sub-key `agents.defaults.sandbox.prune` exists** (visible at Phase 5 schema check) but was deferred at 6a.10 — the §4.1 ask doesn't include prune config, so we left it at default. Colima VM disk is 60GB; not an immediate concern. | **Operational item — monitor and decide cleanup policy by Month 2.** Three options when revisited: (a) configure `agents.defaults.sandbox.prune` (read schema for the policy options — likely `{maxAgeHours, maxCount}` shape or similar), (b) add a Phase 0 cron job that runs `docker container prune --filter 'label=openclaw-sandbox' --filter 'until=24h'` nightly (note: cron is in `tools.deny` per §4.1, so this would be a system-level launchd cron not an agent-driven one), (c) leave at default and revisit only if disk pressure surfaces. **Recommendation:** defer to Phase 1 voice-training session (Week 2+) when we have real session-rollover data. | F34 | Sandbox container runs as host uid:gid (502:20), not the container image's USER directive (1000:1000 sandbox) (added 2026-04-27 at Session 6a.10 Phase 6) | Phase 6 docker inspect on sandbox container `9a685955b735` revealed `Config.User: "502:20"`. Container image `openclaw-sandbox:bookworm-slim` declares `USER 1000:1000` in its Dockerfile (per the 6a.9 smoke test which showed `uid=1000(sandbox)`). The runtime container is invoked with `--user 502:20` overriding the image USER directive, mapping the host openclaw user (`uid=502 staff gid=20`) into the container. Reasoning: the workspace bind mount `/Users/openclaw/.openclaw/workspace-pa:/workspace:z` is owned by `openclaw:staff` (502:20) on the host. If the container ran as 1000:1000 (the image user) it could not write to the workspace bind. By passing through the host uid:gid, the container can read/write the workspace as openclaw, and host-side files written by the agent are owned by the host openclaw user (consistent with the rest of the agent runtime). **This is the correct design** for the sandbox-rw workspace pattern under macOS without rootless docker. Documented for future awareness because: (1) the image's declared sandbox user (uid 1000) is bypassed at runtime — anyone reasoning about "what user does the agent run as inside the sandbox" needs to know it's 502, not 1000; (2) if a future per-agent override sets `agents.defaults.sandbox.docker.user`, it would override this 502:20 default and may break workspace writes; (3) when other agents materialise their workspaces (currently only PA has materialised), each per-agent workspace dir under `~/.openclaw/workspace-<id>/` must be owned by `openclaw:staff` for the same reason. | **No action required** — current state is correct and self-consistent. **Operational rule going forward:** any new per-agent workspace dir created under `~/.openclaw/workspace-<id>/` must be `chown openclaw:staff` (or equivalent) to maintain the sandbox-write capability. The 6.6 mass-`mkdir -p` loop already created the 9 workspaces with correct ownership — no remediation needed. If we ever set `agents.defaults.sandbox.docker.user`, verify against this 502:20 default before doing so; preserving the host uid:gid mapping is the right default unless there's a specific reason to override (e.g. multi-user agent runtimes, which we don't have). **Owner:** me, document for future config edits. **Reference:** Phase 6 docker inspect at 6a.10 — Config.User: "502:20" on container `9a685955b735`. |
| F35 | `ssh -T git@github.com` returns exit code 0 in 2026, not 1 as historical OpenSSH/GitHub docs describe (added 2026-04-27 at Session 6a.11 step 8.7) | Step 8.7 end-to-end verify produced `Hi pfedchen-openclaw! You've successfully authenticated, but GitHub does not provide shell access.` with exit code **0**. Historical behaviour (well-documented in OpenSSH man pages, GitHub Help articles, and a decade of stack-overflow answers): GitHub's SSH endpoint refuses shell access, so SSH exits non-zero (typically 1) even on successful authentication; the success signal is the greeting text, not the exit code. GitHub appears to have changed their handshake-success behaviour at some point — possibly tied to the 2022 RSA-host-key rotation or later. **Functional impact: zero for step 8** — handshake succeeded, key auth chain verified. **Operational implication for any future automation that parses `ssh -T` results:** match on greeting message presence (`Hi <user>! You've successfully authenticated`), not exit status. Exit-code-based logic written against the historical 1-exit will misread the new 0-exit as some other condition (or silently pass when it shouldn't). | **Document for step 15 cron writing.** When the daily git-push cron is authored, any health check that wraps `ssh -T git@github.com` for periodic auth verification must grep the greeting output, not check `$?`. **Owner:** me, surface at step 15. **Reference:** Session 6a.11 step 8.7 output (`exit code: 0`, greeting `Hi pfedchen-openclaw!`). **6a.13 reinforcement:** `ssh -T git@github.com` exit code at 6a.13 sanity batch was **1** (greeting text identical: `Hi pfedchen-openclaw!`). 8.7 captured 0; 6a.13 captures 1. Exit code is unstable across runs even on a single host with no auth changes. The greeting-text-not-exit-code lesson stands and is reinforced: any future automation parsing `ssh -T` output MUST grep for greeting presence, MUST NOT branch on `$?`. Branching on exit code would intermittently fail. **Owner:** me at step 15 cron writing — apply rule rigorously. |

| F38 | `op read | sha256sum` hashes 47 bytes (token + trailing newline); `op read --no-newline | sha256sum` hashes 46 (canonical token only) — different SHAs are NOT a token-mismatch (added 2026-04-28 at Session 6a.13 step 9.3-prelude) | At 9.3-prelude Marie cycle, repeated `op read 'op://OpenClaw/.../token' | sha256sum` returned `91fc1661f1663bc6b7ba0b0743b3eca69655b19769723dc7b195fde26711ab35`; subsequent `BT=$(op read ...); echo -n "$BT" | sha256sum` returned `fe8b0644d66234ce413bbdeeeb1578b9cb6fe2e83d46a08efec0cd1fc249b876` (length 46 in both `wc` checks). Followed by `printf '%s' "$BT" | sha256sum` also returning `fe8b0644...`, ruling out `echo` builtin issues. Followed by `op read --out-file /tmp/op_marie_GmQ1Pu` writing 46 bytes mode 0600 then `sha256sum` of that file also `fe8b0644...`. Diagnostic round to characterise: `op read --no-newline | sha256sum` returns `fe8b0644...` (matches `$BT`); `op read | sha256sum` returns `91fc1661...`; both `wc -c` show 46 and 47 bytes respectively. Same input bytes plus or minus a trailing newline. Resolution: **`op read` appends a trailing `\n` to stdout by default. `$()` strips that newline per zsh spec, leaving `$BT` at 46 bytes. `--out-file` writes raw bytes without the newline. `sha256sum` over a direct pipe hashes the 47 bytes including the appended newline; over a file or `printf '%s' "$BT"` hashes the 46 raw bytes.** The phantom 47-vs-46 mystery resolved cleanly. Real canonical bot-token bytes are 46 (matching Telegram's `<10-digit-bot_id>:<35-char-secret>` format = 46 chars). | **Operational rule:** when locking a token SHA reference, use `op read --no-newline 'op://...' \| sha256sum`. The `--no-newline` flag is canonical — output is raw bytes only, no platform-or-shell-specific newline ambiguity. The 46-byte-canonical reference is the right anchor for verifying the token wrote correctly into a config (config storage doesn't have the trailing newline either). **Sub-fact correction to F2 6a.13 update:** the 47-byte SHAs locked for Charlotte/Andreas/Sophie at 6a.13 (`786258b4...`, `a2f04ed9...`, `8be2667e...`) were captured WITHOUT `--no-newline`, so they are the 47-byte form including the trailing newline. Re-hash the three at 6a.14 prep using `op read --no-newline` to lock the canonical 46-byte references. Marie's 46-byte canonical SHA `fe8b0644d66234ce413bbdeeeb1578b9cb6fe2e83d46a08efec0cd1fc249b876` is locked. **Reusable diagnostic pattern:** when `wc -c` reports byte counts that differ by exactly 1 between `$VAR` and direct-pipe-from-source, suspect the trailing-newline class of issues first. `printf '%s'` for variable contents and `--no-newline` flags on source commands eliminate the ambiguity. **Owner:** me at 6a.14 prep — re-hash 3 bots; document operational rule for any future credential SHA work. **Reference:** Session 6a.13 diagnostic round at 9.3-prelude. **6a.14 closure narrative + 6a.15 reinforcement — F38 CLOSED.** At 6a.14 9.3a: 3 SHAs re-hashed via `op read --no-newline | sha256sum`, all 4 canonical 46-byte references locked. At 6a.15 9.3b: pattern reused × 4 (one per bot cycle) — every pre-flight read produced exactly 46-byte output with SHA matching locked reference; every post-add inspection re-computed botToken SHA and matched same locked reference. Pattern is now standing discipline. **Sub-fact addition for op CLI session lifecycle:** op session expires after ~30 minutes idle (default for `my.1password.eu` shard). Pattern: pre-flight `op whoami | grep -E "URL|Email" || { echo "OP NOT AUTH"; exit 1 }` at every state-changing op-touching block. If session expired, `eval $(op signin)` (interactive — prompts for master password). At 6a.15 9.3b for Charlotte: first attempt failed silently — op session had expired between Marie's cycle (~09:35) and Charlotte's start (~10:07); BT was set to empty string, channels-add rejected with `Telegram requires token`, defensive Python assertion `channels-add did not create pro record` correctly aborted the edit cycle. Zero state damage; cycle re-ran cleanly after `eval $(op signin)`. F38 closes. |

Mental model tightened: live config `auth` block contains zero credential fields. **Pattern lesson:** for any future "is this field null vs absent" check, prefer Python `.get(key, sentinel)` over `jq -r` — sentinel comparison is unambiguous.
