| F47 | gog 0.14.0 `gog backup` framework architecturally GitHub-centric; blocks local-only Phase D adoption (added 2026-05-03 at Session 6a.19 path (b') diagnostic round) | **Empirical evidence — three failures of progressively-narrower scope at 6a.19:** (1) `gog -a pfedchen@gmail.com backup init --repo /tmp/gog-backup-init-dryrun --no-push --dry-run --verbose` → `Username for 'https://github.com':` interactive prompt fired despite `--dry-run` + `--no-push`. Aborted via Ctrl+C. (2) Same invocation + `--no-input < /dev/null` → same prompt fired despite the flag and stdin redirect. Aborted. (3) `gog -a pfedchen@gmail.com backup status --no-input < /dev/null` (read-only manifest inspection per `--help`) → same prompt fired. **All three failures point to gog reaching out to a github.com remote URL even for nominally-local operations.** **Configuration audit ruled out hidden defaults:** `~/Library/Application Support/gogcli/` contains only `credentials.json` + `keyring/` (verified at 6a.19 sanity batch — no `config.json`, no `backup.json`, no JSON5 config); `git config --global --list` returned only `user.name=OpenClaw Mac Mini` + `user.email=openclaw.pfedchen@gmail.com` (zero `credential.helper`, zero URL rewrites — git is not the source of the github prompt); `gog config keys` returned only `timezone` / `keyring_backend` / `gmail_no_send` (no `backup_remote` or similar override knob); `gog config list` shows all three keys `(not set)`. No on-disk state explains the github default. **README + CHANGELOG analysis confirms architectural posture:** `gog backup` shipped as 0.14.0's headline feature 6 days ago (2026-04-28). Full 1779-line README reading: README's Commands section enumerates every other subcommand group (Authentication, Gmail, Calendar, Drive, Docs/Slides/Sheets, etc.) but has zero `gog backup` documentation — likely lives in `docs/backup.md` (other subcommands follow this pattern: `docs/watch.md`, `docs/email-tracking.md`, etc.) but `docs/backup.md` is not directly fetchable via web_fetch. Available search snippets describing `gog backup` cite GitHub-centric examples exclusively (`gog backup init --repo ~/Projects/backup-gog --remote https://github.com/steipete/backup-gog.git`); the security framing in available snippets reads "GitHub only receives public age1... recipients, manifest.json, and encrypted *.jsonl.gz.age payloads" + "Security boundary: GitHub cannot read Google content without the age identity" — both frame GitHub as the assumed remote, not "git remote" generically. **Architectural conclusion (high confidence):** gogcli 0.14.0's `gog backup` framework is designed assuming a github.com remote; the framework appears to invoke `git fetch` / `git ls-remote` against the configured remote URL on every operation (including read-only `status` and `--dry-run`) to keep manifest.json in sync. When `--remote` is absent at the CLI, gog falls back to a hardcoded github URL pattern, which triggers git's interactive credential prompt. No documented `--no-remote` flag, no documented `file://` scheme support surfaced in 5+ sources searched. Framework may support local-only operation but not in any documented or empirically-verifiable way at 6a.19. | **Resolution path (deferred to Librarian week 6):** Three sub-paths if pursued at Librarian phase: **(i)** clone gogcli source at `git@github.com:steipete/gogcli.git` locally, read `docs/backup.md` directly + grep source for `--remote` handling logic, characterise empirically whether file:// URLs are actually supported but undocumented; **(ii)** file an issue upstream at `github.com/steipete/gogcli/issues` requesting documented local-only / file:// remote operation, and provide repro of the 6a.19 empirical failures — likely cheap if maintainer responsive; **(iii)** if (i)/(ii) surface a viable path, contribute a PR adding `--no-remote` flag or documenting file:// support. **Owner:** deferred to Librarian build session (week 6+) when Workspace + git infrastructure already authored and Phase G has surfaced cloud-push policy decisions. **F47 closure path:** when `gog backup` framework can be operated purely locally (file:// remote OR `--no-remote` flag OR documented zero-remote mode), F47 closes with the empirical winning configuration locked. Library's WSGI handler logs the full request line per stdlib logging convention; no clean opt-out without subclassing the formatter or filter. **Mitigation applied at 6a.20:** post-bootstrap script patch added `LOG_FILE.touch + os.chmod(LOG_FILE, 0o600)` lines between `BACKUP_DIR.mkdir` and `logging.basicConfig` — log file now mode 0600 staff (same as backup files + token file). Filesystem permission is the practical defense; auth codes only enter the log on first-run bootstrap or refresh-token-expiry-needs-rebootstrap events, so the per-run secret-leak rate is low after the first run. | **Resolution path:** **(i)** filesystem 0600 mitigation in place — sufficient for solo-use Mac Mini context where openclaw user owns the file and no other user can read it. **(ii)** if F49 ever bites in shared/multi-user context, mitigations include: (a) subclassing `logging.Filter` to redact `code=...&` patterns from log records before emission (~10 lines of code, drop into script's setup_logging); (b) configuring the google-auth-oauthlib logger explicitly to WARNING level only, preventing INFO-level GET line emission entirely; (c) routing the library's logger to a separate FileHandler that gets immediately deleted post-bootstrap. **(iii)** F49 might also be filed as upstream improvement-request issue at `googleapis/google-auth-library-python-oauthlib` since logging the full GET line is a defensible default for HTTP server-debug visibility but suboptimal for library-as-OAuth-flow use; lower priority. **Owner:** me at any future session if F49 mitigation proves insufficient (e.g., audit requirement surfaces); otherwise stays closed-with-mitigation. **F49 closure path:** F49 closes when (i) log-file mode 0600 is verified preserved across script test-runs (already the case at 6a.20 post-patch); (ii) operational confidence accumulates that auth-code in a 0600 file is acceptable risk in solo-use context. | F55 | macOS Tahoe `crontab -` write fails from SSH with "Operation not permitted" due to TCC sandboxing of the cron daemon — added 2026-05-05 at Session 6a.23 Stage 5.B.1.C | **Empirical evidence at 6a.23 Stage 5.B.1.C:** `crontab -` invocation from SSH session as openclaw user with stdin redirection of a 2-line cron schedule (calendar-backup at 4am + security audit at 6am) failed with `crontab: tmp/tmp.72198: Operation not permitted` and exit code 1. Pre-anchors and post-anchors confirmed zero state mutation: openclaw.json + models.json sha12 unchanged across the failed write attempt; `crontab -l` before AND after returned "no crontab for openclaw" — the failed write left no partial state. **Asymmetry confirmed**: `crontab -l` (read) succeeded earlier in the session at Stage 5.B.0.A returning "no crontab for openclaw" cleanly without permission errors; only `crontab -` (write) is blocked. **Root cause (high confidence):** macOS Tahoe / Sequoia hardens TCC (Transparency, Consent, Control) sandboxing of the `cron` daemon and the `crontab` write tool. The write path drops a temporary file under `/var/at/tmp/` (the path "tmp/tmp.72198" in the error message is `crontab`'s internal cwd-relative target inside that protected root), which requires Full Disk Access (FDA) permission grant for the parent process. From an SSH context, the parent is `sshd` which doesn't have FDA by default. From a Terminal.app GUI context, Terminal needs an explicit FDA grant via System Settings → Privacy & Security → Full Disk Access. Both grants require GUI-session access which itself is GUI-session-bound per D20's same-pattern restriction (LaunchAgent install requires GUI session; TCC permission grants likewise). **Architectural implication**: modern macOS deprecates user-cron in favor of launchd LaunchAgents for scheduled tasks. cron technically still works in 2026.4 but is increasingly TCC-restricted. Pivoting to launchd is the canonical path. But launchd LaunchAgent install/bootstrap is GUI-session-bound per D20. | F60 | `.last-good` poisoning + 3a rollback incident (6a.27) | During the 6a.27 Stage 3a `provider:"local"` write+revert, the FIRST rollback restored from a poisoned source: `openclaw.json.last-good` was **7401B / memorySearch=1** (PATCHED content, not the clean 7285B original) — the v5 apply script's refresh-in-place of `.last-good` had captured patched bytes, so the broken config was "restored" onto itself. Recovery succeeded ONLY because the immutable per-run timestamped backup `openclaw.json.bak-6a27-3a-20260517-202327` (verified 7285B / memorySearch=0 / valid JSON) was intact. A corrected rollback hard-gated the restore source on exact size/content/JSON-validity before touching live, atomically restored, byte-compared result to source, and repaired the poisoned `.last-good` from the verified clean source. Final: live 7285B byte-identical to clean anchor, `.last-good` repaired (7285B/mem=0), `Config valid`, gateway 5846→6188 healthz 200, 9 agents `bedrock(auto)`, no `Unknown provider`. Three rollback-script bugs surfaced — **NONE reached live** (caught by sandbox or the script's own hard gate): false line-granularity additive guard; `grep -c … || echo 99` multiline; **BSD `wc` leading-space padding**. | **Closed at 6a.27 — system verified known-good; net config change zero.** **LESSON (high-priority): the immutable per-run timestamped backup is the trustworthy rollback anchor; a refreshed-in-place `.last-good` is NOT.** Future state-changing writes must (a) immutable timestamped backup BEFORE mutation, (b) hard-gate every restore on exact expected size/content/JSON-validity (strip whitespace, integer compare — BSD-safe), (c) never trust `.last-good` without that gate. **Secondary: sandbox with BSD-tool emulation by default**; zsh mangles multi-line heredocs + multibyte base64 (a Python file corrupted twice in transit) → deliver scripts as **SHA-256-verified files**. **Forensic artifacts on the Mini (do NOT delete):** `openclaw.json.bak-6a27-3a-20260517-202327` (clean 7285B anchor — saved the recovery), `openclaw.json.bak-6a27-3a-PRE-ROLLBACK-20260517-204158` (broken 7401B copy). 6a.28 pre-flight MUST re-verify `.last-good` cleanliness (if 7401/mem=1, poisoning recurred — STOP). **Cross-ref:** D22 6a.27 RESOLUTION; S6 4th instance; SESSION-6a27-CLOSURE.md §4. |

The validation step that was missing: tail of `calendar-backup-cron.log` to confirm *what the script actually does on a fire* would have shown a `google-auth-oauthlib` refresh-failure traceback at 6a.29 (the first 04:00 fire after Stage 3b was 2026-05-20 04:00, which logged `invalid_grant: Token has been expired or revoked.` — fully observable in the log, never inspected). **Carry-forward rule:** post-Stage-3b-class verification for any launchd job must include log-tail of the job's stdout/stderr path after at least one fire window has passed, not just `launchctl print` of the loaded state. Sanity-batch design for sessions with active scheduled jobs should include log-tail + output-existence checks, not just plist + env state. **Cross-ref:** F44 (real failure mode), F64 NEW (script hang bug surfaced at same investigation), D17 (Python-bypass architecture that F63 misdiagnosis missed), SESSION-6a30-CLOSURE.md §F63-correction. **6a.31 — Carry-forward rule fired correctly; first TRUE F63-class instance surfaced; lineage extended proactively.** The log-tail + output-existence carry-forward rule (added at 6a.30 CORRECTION) was implemented in `sanity_6a31.py` and caught **F68 NEW** at 6a.31 Stage 0 pre-flight: security-audit launchd job had been silently failing every fire since 2026-05-20 with `env: node: No such file or directory`. F63 itself was MISDIAGNOSED at 6a.29 (calendar-backup uses Python-bypass auth per D17, doesn't consume shell env); F68 is the **first TRUE F63-class instance** (security-audit DOES shell out to node which lives at /opt/homebrew/bin/node, absent from launchd PATH). The generalised lesson — verify the consuming context's actual environment, don't assume shell env propagates — was then applied PROACTIVELY at Stage 5 design to identify **F70 NEW** (op CLI launchd env-gap; OP_SESSION token in interactive shell, absent from launchd context). F63 lineage now: F63 (misdiagnosed) → F68 (first real instance, surfaced after silent failure) → F70 (proactive prevention before silent failure). **Cross-ref:** F68 NEW; F70 NEW; D24 6a.31 ENFORCEMENT; SESSION-6a31-CLOSURE.md §F68-discovery + §Stage-5-MVP-design.
| F64 | `calendar-backup.py` refresh-failure fallthrough starts InstalledAppFlow.run_local_server() which hangs forever in non-interactive launchd context (surfaced 2026-05-23 at Session 6a.30 F63.4 pre-flight) | **Empirical evidence at 6a.30 F63.4 pre-flight:** `launchctl print gui/502/ai.openclaw.calendar-backup` showed `state = running` despite no scheduled-fire window in the next 17h. Investigation: `ps auxww` revealed PID 12523 (CommandLineTools Python 3.9 + `calendar-backup.py`) alive since "Fri 04 a.m." = 2026-05-22 04:00 BST, ~31 hours wall-clock, ~46MB RSS. `tail -100 ~/.openclaw/logs/calendar-backup-cron.log` showed pattern: 2026-05-20 04:00:01 `refresh failed: invalid_grant: Token has been expired or revoked.; falling through to bootstrap` → `Please visit this URL to authorize this application: https://accounts.google.com/o/oauth2/auth?...&redirect_uri=http%3A%2F%2Flocalhost%3A8765%2F...`. Same pattern repeats at 2026-05-22 04:00:02. NO 2026-05-21 entry (launchd default `state=running` prevents re-fire of an already-running job → 2026-05-20's hung process blocked 2026-05-21; 2026-05-20's process eventually terminated for unknown reason allowing 2026-05-22 to fire; 2026-05-22's process is the current hang). **Root cause:** the script's refresh-failure code path falls through to `InstalledAppFlow.run_local_server(port=8765, open_browser=False)` (per D17 Phase-D bootstrap design at 6a.20 — the first-run interactive OAuth flow). In a launchd 04:00 context with no human at a browser, the local HTTP server on 8765 blocks forever waiting for an OAuth callback that never arrives. **Impact:** every F44 token-expiry cycle (~7 days under External/Testing posture) triggers a hung Python process holding port 8765 + ~46MB RSS until manually killed; launchd schedule effectively becomes single-shot until manual intervention. Backup files: last successful 2026-05-05 (matches F44 history); no successful runs since the 2026-05-19 Stage 3b bootstrap. | **Filing-priority LOW** (job descoped at 6a.30 per D24; this bug doesn't bite while descoped). **Resolution at re-enable** (calendar-backup re-enable session, ~2 months post-6a.30 per D24 trigger): script must distinguish first-run-bootstrap context from scheduled-refresh context, and on refresh-failure in scheduled context must fail-fast and exit non-zero, NOT start a local HTTP server. Suggested fix shape: gate the `InstalledAppFlow.run_local_server()` path behind an explicit `--bootstrap` CLI flag (or an `OPENCLAW_CALENDAR_BACKUP_BOOTSTRAP=1` env var) that the launchd plist does NOT pass; scheduled runs without that flag should `log.error` + `sys.exit(1)` on refresh failure. Additionally: launchd plist could add `AbandonProcessGroup=true` + a `RunAtLoad` retry, or a wrapper that enforces a hard timeout via `gtimeout` (note F60 caveat — macOS lacks `timeout`; use Python signal-based wrapper instead). **F44 + F63 are upstream of F64** in the sense that F64 only matters when refresh fails (F44) AND launchd is the consumer (F63's domain). At re-enable, picking option (b) macOS Keychain backend for credential storage AND fixing F64 fail-fast semantics AND deciding the Workspace topology are three separate changes that all need to land together. **Process artifacts (6a.30):** log-tail output preserved in SESSION-6a30-CLOSURE.md §F64-discovery; `ps auxww | grep calendar-backup` PID 12523 cleared via F63.4 bootout. **Cross-ref:** F44, F63 (6a.30 CORRECTION segment), D17, D24, SESSION-6a30-CLOSURE.md §F64-discovery + §descope. **6a.31 — Reaffirmed superseded-by-disposition.** Calendar-backup descope mechanism (D24 ENFORCEMENT at 6a.31 via rename to `.disabled-D24`) is durable through forced reboot; F64 hang bug stays dormant until calendar-backup re-enable. **Cross-ref:** D24 6a.31 ENFORCEMENT.
| F65 | Obsidian Sync excludes dot-files by default; `_Private/.obsidian-ignore` marker placed on MacBook did NOT propagate to Mini at Stage 4.5 (surfaced 6a.30 Stage 4.5 verification) | **Empirical evidence at 6a.30 Stage 4.5:** marker file `.obsidian-ignore` placed at `/Users/pfedchenkov/obsidian-vault/_Private/.obsidian-ignore` on MacBook, then Sync enabled and verified up-to-date; on Mini, `ls -la /Users/openclaw/obsidian-vault/_Private/` showed `total 0` (no marker). Documented Obsidian Sync behaviour: dot-files are excluded from sync by default (operating-system metadata like `.DS_Store`, editor swap files, hidden artefacts); ONLY `.obsidian/` itself is special-cased to sync. The exclusion is product-design, not defect. | **Disposition: NOT a defect, but a planning miss at 6a.30 Stage 4 scope.** Documentation-class artefacts intended to exist on a SPECIFIC device (e.g., Mini-side metadata for Docker mount spec readers) must be placed via SSH directly on that device, not via vault Sync. **Action taken at 6a.30:** marker placed on Mini directly via `cat > .../.obsidian-ignore`; Mini-local marker is the right scope (the consumer is the Librarian build's Docker volume spec, which reads Mini paths, not MacBook). **Sync test executed** (created `_TEMP/sync-test.md` on MacBook, verified propagation to Mini within ~30s, then deleted; deletion also propagated) to confirm Sync DOES work for content files (non-dot-prefixed). **Carry-forward rule:** vault-level metadata that must exist on a specific device requires direct SSH placement; vault-level CONTENT propagates via Sync as expected. Future agent-Docker-mount config and any device-local convention markers follow the same pattern. **Cross-ref:** Stage 4.5 line 443 step 17; SESSION-6a30-CLOSURE.md §Stage-4. |
| F66 | openclaw user login Keychain created at mode 644, not 600 (observed both original 20260430-created Keychain and 20260523-22:29-regenerated Keychain at Stage 4.5 Keychain diagnosis) | **Empirical evidence at 6a.30 Stage 4.5:** `ls -la /Users/openclaw/Library/Keychains/` showed `-rw-r--r--@ 1 openclaw staff 36972 23 May 21:11 login.keychain-db` (pre-regeneration) and `-rw-r--r-- 1 openclaw staff 32824 23 May 22:29 login.keychain-db` (post-regeneration after fix path 2 + physical login). Both mode 644 (world-readable), not the expected 600 (owner-only). Affects only the openclaw service account's Keychain on this Mini; the pre-existing pfedchenkov admin account's Keychain not inspected. | **Disposition: accepted at 6a.30 without remediation.** Reasoning: (1) Mini is single-tenant-in-practice (no other meaningful local Unix users besides pfedchenkov admin); (2) Keychain contents are encrypted at rest -- file readability without password yields encrypted blob, not secrets; (3) root cause is likely macOS Tahoe-era default behaviour, NOT a setup defect (regenerated Keychain via standard logout-login flow exhibited identical perms, ruling out non-standard creation hypothesis); (4) manual `chmod 600` would be a maintenance chore re-required after every Keychain regeneration, with no clear benefit on single-tenant Mini. **Re-evaluate at:** (a) any future change in Mini's user model (additional accounts added); (b) any future audit requirement that Mini's openclaw Keychain perms be hardened; (c) macOS major-version upgrade may regenerate or change Keychain perms behaviour. **Process note:** L-β symptom (Keychain Access GUI rejecting current login password) at 6a.30 was a SEPARATE issue, not caused by the perms; resolved by Keychain regeneration via fix path 2. The repeating-Obsidian-prompts behaviour also resolved post-regeneration (fresh empty Keychain has no entries needing access authorization). **Cross-ref:** F67 (fix-path-2 headless-Mini risk); SESSION-6a30-CLOSURE.md §Stage-4-Keychain. |
| F67 | Headless Mini risk: user-session-state mutations requiring logout-and-back-in for recovery need GUI access; SSH alone cannot complete (surfaced 6a.30 Stage 4 Keychain fix path 2) | **Empirical evidence at 6a.30:** Stage 4 Keychain L-β diagnosis chose fix path 2 (`mv login.keychain-db .../login.keychain-db.broken-<ts>` + logout + login → new Keychain auto-created with current login password). The logout step was completed via SSH; subsequent Screen Sharing connection failed because no authenticated session existed for Screen Sharing to attach to. Recovery required physical access to the Mini (monitor + keyboard + login physically as openclaw) to complete the macOS GUI login flow that creates the new Keychain. Post-physical-login, SSH and Screen Sharing both recovered automatically. | **OPEN -- carry-forward rule, not a session-blocker now.** Future user-session-state mutations on headless Mini (Keychain reset, FileVault changes, password reset, login-shell changes affecting auto-login, etc.) must verify GUI access AVAILABLE-AND-TESTED before mutating, OR sequence the mutation such that recovery path doesn't require physical access (e.g., complete the GUI step before any teardown; or set up a remote-management out-of-band mechanism). **Process miss at 6a.30:** Claude offered fix path 2 (mv + logout + login) without flagging that the logout-and-back-in step is GUI-only on a headless device. Should have either (a) recommended fix path 1 (`security set-keychain-password`) which is SSH-completable, OR (b) explicit precondition check 'do you have physical access available if we need it', OR (c) explicit pause-discipline gate before the mv command 'this commits you to physical-access recovery if Screen Sharing fails post-logout.' **Carry-forward into sanity-batch design:** any future Mini setup-state checklist should include a 'remote management resilient against my own mistakes' validation -- e.g., a known-good alternate-user SSH path that doesn't depend on openclaw being logged in. **Cross-ref:** F66 (Keychain perms accepted-as-Apple-default); D20 (gateway lifecycle SSH-vs-GUI constraint, related but distinct -- D20 is about launchctl, F67 is about user-session auth); SESSION-6a30-CLOSURE.md §Stage-4-Keychain. **6a.31 — GUI Terminal launchctl authority restored post-reboot; sub-lesson NEW.** Saturday 6a.30 close noted launchctl `bootstrap`/`bootout` from openclaw GUI Terminal returning `Bad request.` even though same SSH-as-openclaw context could read launchctl state; initially conjectured as Tahoe-quirk. Post-forced-reboot at 6a.31 resumption (2026-06-01), bootstrap of Stage 4.8 `ai.openclaw.vault-backup.plist` from openclaw GUI Terminal succeeded cleanly (D-1 block: `bootstrap exit=0`, service properly enumerated in gui/502 — see SESSION-6a31-CLOSURE.md §Stage-4.8). Conclusion: the 6a.30 `Bad request.` behaviour was specific to the unusual post-physical-Keychain-recovery session state (22:29 BST 2026-05-23), not a Tahoe-universal regression. **F69 NEW** (leading-line `Bad request.` convention + `| head -1` truncation trap) still applies for parsing launchctl error output. **F67 sub-lesson NEW at 6a.31:** login re-loads `~/Library/LaunchAgents/*.plist` regardless of prior gui/<uid> bootout state. Durable removal requires the plist file out of LaunchAgents/ OR with a non-`*.plist` suffix. Bootout alone is gui/<uid>-session-scoped, not persistent across logins. This sub-lesson informed Finding-E disposition (rename to `.disabled-D24` mechanism at 6a.31). **Cross-ref:** F69 NEW; D24 6a.31 ENFORCEMENT; SESSION-6a31-CLOSURE.md §post-reboot-sanity + §Finding-E.
| F68 | security-audit launchd job env-gap: `env: node: No such file or directory` on every fire since 2026-05-20 06:00 (surfaced 6a.31 Stage 0 pre-flight via F63 6a.30 CORRECTION carry-forward rule) | **Empirical evidence at 6a.31 Stage 0:** `sanity_6a31.py` (sha256 `2eefbcb98eebcbe2257c3be93c2624e134b19d04275761e737be54d0e987f6c2`) implemented the F63 6a.30 CORRECTION rule — log-tail check on scheduled jobs, not just `launchctl print` of loaded state. `ai.openclaw.security-audit` plist (sha12 `63ffb23f60e1`) discovered to set StandardOutPath = StandardErrorPath = `/Users/openclaw/.openclaw/logs/security-audit-cron.log`. Log tail revealed 5 consecutive identical entries: `env: node: No such file or directory` for fires at 2026-05-20 / 21 / 22 / 23 at 06:00 BST. Zero successful runs since Stage 3b placement at 6a.29 (4 fires before 6a.30 Keychain reboot, all failed; 0 fires post-relogin window before 6a.31). Root cause: launchd `gui/<uid>` execution context has minimal PATH (`/usr/bin:/bin:/usr/sbin:/sbin`); `node` lives at `/opt/homebrew/bin/node` (brew-installed), absent from launchd PATH. The security-audit invocation chain (via `openclaw security audit ...`) shells out to `node` for the openclaw runtime CLI; `env: node` is the env-prefix wrapper's failure. **This is the first TRUE F63-class env-gap** — F63 itself was misdiagnosed at 6a.29 because calendar-backup.py doesn't use shell env (per D17 Python-bypass); security-audit DOES use shell-PATH-resolved node. The carry-forward rule worked as designed: surfaced this in 6a.31 pre-flight, one session after the rule was added. **Process win:** scheduled-job verification rule applied prophylactically, caught silent failure. **Process miss (6a.29):** sanity batch did NOT include log-tail; rule was added at 6a.30 but only applied at 6a.31; security-audit failed silently for 4 fires. | **DESCOPED at 6a.31 via D24-symmetric mechanism.** Reasoning parallels D24: at pre-6b, no agent consumer of security-audit output exists (CoS / Sophie at 6b+ are the eventual consumers); 4 weeks of silent failure suggests no one was reading the output; "place the scheduled job when the consumer exists" lesson (6a.30) applies. F68 CLOSED-AS-DESCOPED-SYMMETRIC-TO-D24. Mechanism: `launchctl bootout gui/502/ai.openclaw.security-audit` + rename `~/Library/LaunchAgents/ai.openclaw.security-audit.plist` → `ai.openclaw.security-audit.plist.disabled-D24` (preserves sha12 `63ffb23f60e1` content, breaks launchd auto-load on next user login per F67 sub-lesson). **Re-open trigger:** at first agent consumer build (CoS or Sophie at 6b+); pick remediation: (a) plist `EnvironmentVariables` adding `/opt/homebrew/bin` to PATH (surgical, low-risk, applies F63 lesson explicitly) OR (b) replace `node` invocation with absolute `/opt/homebrew/bin/node` in the security-audit invocation chain OR (c) wrapper script with hardcoded PATH preamble — (a) is the cleanest fix. At re-enable: apply F63 6a.30 CORRECTION carry-forward rule (verify log-tail post-bootstrap, not just loaded state) AND F67 sub-lesson (durable removal requires non-`*.plist` suffix in disabled state). **Cross-ref:** F63 (env-gap class; F68 is first true instance); D24 6a.31 ENFORCEMENT (symmetric descope reasoning); F67 sub-lesson (rename mechanism for durable descope); F69 (Tahoe `Bad request.` leading-line obscured bootout-success during disposition); F70 (op CLI launchd env-gap, identified proactively in same lineage); SESSION-6a31-CLOSURE.md §F68-discovery. |
| F69 | Tahoe `launchctl` emits cryptic `Bad request.` as stderr leading line for several failure modes; actual diagnostic message follows on line 2 (surfaced 6a.31 Finding-E disposition Block 2/Block 3) | **Empirical evidence at 6a.31:** during Finding-E disposition (re-bootout of calendar-backup + security-audit jobs at Block 2), `launchctl print gui/502/ai.openclaw.calendar-backup 2>&1 | head -1` returned only the cryptic line `Bad request.` from openclaw GUI Terminal — initially read as a failure-to-execute symptom; appeared to fire on every print AND bootout invocation; same from openclaw GUI Terminal AND from pfedchenkov SSH `sudo launchctl print`. Workaround path (admin sudo + `| head -3`) revealed line 2 = `Could not find service "ai.openclaw.<label>" in domain for user gui: 502` — the actual launchd-v2 diagnostic showing the service was successfully unloaded. The bootouts at Block 2 had in fact SUCCEEDED (the `Bad request.` was misleading framing decoration over a clean success: target removed, no longer in gui/502); the `| head -1` in my own diagnostic instructions truncated line 2 and hid the actual state from view. After this realisation, Block 3 (rename + verify) used `| head -3` and observed proper `Bad request.` (line 1) + `Could not find service` (line 2) pair confirming durable unload-then-rename state. | **Carry-forward rule (OPEN):** launchctl error parsing must use `| head -3` or more, NEVER `| head -1`. Truncating to line 1 hides the actual diagnostic. Applies retroactively: `sanity_6a31.py` runtime-one-liners for calendar-backup + security-audit launchctl probes correctly use `| head -3` (the script's emit was right; my interactive Block 2 verifies were wrong with `| head -1` — captured process miss). Future sanity-script designs for any session that introspects launchctl state must respect this minimum. **Disposition: OPEN as carry-forward rule** — Tahoe launchctl semantics are not changeable; the rule is about how operators (and future Claude instances) read launchctl output. The behavior may extend beyond `Could not find service` to other error categories not yet enumerated; conservative minimum is `head -3`. **Cross-ref:** F60 (sanity-script hygiene); F63 6a.30 CORRECTION (log-tail carry-forward rule that this complements); D20 (gui/<uid> domain semantics that motivated launchctl probes); SESSION-6a31-CLOSURE.md §Finding-E. |
| F70 | `op` CLI in launchd-spawned context will not be authenticated; OP_SESSION_<id> token lives only in interactive shell env, absent from plist EnvironmentVariables; daily Stage 5 1Password backup automation cannot run headless via launchd without separate auth mechanism (surfaced 6a.31 Stage 5 design proactively) | **Pre-emptive identification at 6a.31 Stage 5 design:** before writing the Stage 5 backup launchd plist, recognized that the planned `op-backup.sh` script would call `op item list` + `op item get` 35× per fire — and that `op whoami` would fail at the first call in launchd context because the OP_SESSION_my token (set by interactive `eval $(op signin)`) does not propagate to launchd-spawned processes. Peter runs on-demand (weekly, post-credential-rotation, etc.). Stage 6 audit re-scope picks up the automation design question with proper budget. ## Open decisions for Sessions 6b / 6c / 6d

## Strategic risks + scheduled future work

_Items that don't fit the per-session D-row / F-row format because they're system-level concerns, not deviations from spec or empirically-encountered flags. Captured here so they're carried forward in every session opener via DEVIATIONS-LOG attachment. Each item: name, what it is, mitigation plan, target timeframe/session, current status. Added 2026-05-03 at 6a.20 close after Peter's "what about big risks" strategic review._

### S1 — Phase G resequencing: land BEFORE 6b PA build
- **What it is:** Phase G (fedchenkov.com Workspace setup; closes F44 by flipping OAuth consent screen from External/Testing to Internal) was originally sequenced as "own session whenever convenient." F44's External/Testing posture forces 7-day refresh-token expiry on ALL OAuth grants (gog PA + gog ProA + calendar-backup-token.json). Once 6b lands and PA starts running daily via Telegram, Marie's gog-routed gmail/calendar reads will fail every 7 days unless re-bootstrapped. Same constraint hits the calendar-backup cron job once it's scheduled at 6a.22. **Operational consequence: Phase G after 6b means weekly maintenance burden until Phase G lands.**
- **Mitigation:** resequence Phase G to land BETWEEN 6a.24 (memory verification) AND 6b (PA build). Phase G touches Google Workspace admin + DNS records at registrar (apex MX, team. subdomain MX, SPF, DKIM, DMARC) + OAuth consent screen Internal-flip + test-user posture. ~60-90 min session per STEP-11-12-GMAIL-CALENDAR-PLAN.md Phase G section.
- **Target:** **6a.26 combined Screen Sharing session** per 4-session 6a-tier plan finalised at 6a.23 close. Phase G is combined with F55 launchd bootstrap into a single Screen Sharing trip (saves one trip; both require physical/Screen-Sharing access to Mini); cron infrastructure lands BEFORE 6a.27 gate so the gate's Lesson #10 audit can confirm no implicit-but-untracked scheduled-jobs mandates remain. Original framing was "between 6a.24 and 6b" — superseded by explicit 6a.26 sequencing.
- **Owner:** Peter (S1 is a sequencing decision rather than a recurring-cadence or scheduled-date item; not in CoS's project-manager scope per D19).
- **Status:** OPEN — original sequencing assumed Phase G could slot in at any convenient point; revised at 6a.20 close to land before agents start running daily. **Update this sequencing in any session opener that references "Phase G own session whenever Workspace setup is convenient" — that framing is now superseded.** **6a.26 update —** Phase G slipped 6a.26 → **6a.27** (6a.26 cleanly cut Stage 3 whole on budget after an unbudgeted-but-necessary inter-session-state investigation; clean cut > rushed Phase G on fumes). Phase G + F55 launchd + D22 (now a decision-gate, see D22 row) + F44 closure all land at 6a.27 Stage 3. Still BEFORE 6b PA build — S1's core constraint (Phase G before agents run daily) holds. **6a.32 (A-3):** SUPERSEDED by D24 — Phase G deliberately deferred to post-6b; agents run Day-0 on existing accounts; the "before agents run daily" framing is overtaken; risk ACCEPTED with Day-0-topology mitigation. F45 row says "deferred to whichever 6a-tier session first needs gateway uptime (likely 6a.22 cluster B)." Each session this is deferred, the resolution path becomes slightly more uncertain (was the SIGTERM truly D15 keychain-recreate collateral damage, or has something else degraded since? D11 hasn't manifested per uptime check, but the system's been running 14+ days now without restart).
- **Mitigation:** if 6a.22 is more than ~5-7 days from 6a.20 close (i.e., past ~10 May 2026), run F45 as a standalone 15-min mini-session sooner. Restoration ceremony per F45 row resolution path (`launchctl bootstrap` + `kickstart`). No reason to bundle it with cluster B's cron-jobs work if cluster B's timing slips.
- **Target:** by ~10 May 2026 at outside; ideally as 6a.22 opener if 6a.22 lands sooner.
- **Owner:** Peter through 6a.22 (F45 should close at 6a.22 opener before CoS workspace authored at 6c). If F45 slips past 6a.22 and CoS becomes operational before F45 closes, ownership transfers to Andreas/CoS per D19.

### S3 — D18 Python EOL migration: target by Sept-Oct 2026
- **What it is:** Calendar-backup pipeline runs on Apple system Python 3.9.6 (EOL since October 2025). Google libraries support 3.9 on "best-effort critical bug fixes only" basis. Realistic failure mode: 6-12 months out, transitive dep update (probably `cryptography` or `urllib3`) drops 3.9 entirely; next pip-upgrade breaks imports silently; calendar backup stops working without obvious failure signal until backup is actually needed.
- **Mitigation:** install Homebrew python@3.13 as `pfedchenkov` admin; recreate calendar-backup user-site under Homebrew Python; edit script shebang to explicit `/opt/homebrew/bin/python3.13`; test-run; verify same-shape backup output. ~30-45 min dedicated session per D18 row resolution path.
- **Target:** by mid-2026 outside, ideally September-October 2026 for buffer. Calendar reminder advisable.
- **Owner:** Peter through 6c, then transfers to Andreas/CoS per D19 once CoS workspace authored. CoS tracks the Sept-Oct 2026 target date + drafts execution proposal as date approaches; Peter executes (state-changing brew install + interpreter swap + script shebang edit).
- **Status:** OPEN as D18 NEW. Soft deadline; not blocking anything until transitive deps actually break.

Written for an intelligent operator with ZERO prior context. ~2-3 hours of focused work.

Original framing was "between 6a.24 and Phase G OR between Phase G and 6b" — superseded by explicit 6a.25 sequencing. Doc produced at 6a.25 reflects pre-Phase-G state; will need light post-Phase-G refresh to reflect Workspace-flip outcome (captured as deliverable of 6a.27 gate session sub-check (f)(i) — "S4 5-page operator onramp exists, current as of 6a.27 close").
- **Owner:** Peter (authoring the state-of-nation doc itself is bus-factor mitigation work; CoS doesn't yet exist when the doc is authored). Once authored + CoS operational, the doc becomes a CoS-maintained reference (CoS updates relevant sections post-execution of any M-item or S-item per D19 audit-trail responsibility); D19's project-manager role naturally extends to keeping state-of-nation doc current.
- **Status:** **SUBSTANTIVELY DELIVERED 2026-05-15 at Session 6a.25 Stage 3.** Authored as the planned 5-page operator onramp, then — per Peter's losslessness-conditional directive (\"If you can split without losing any context or important things in the docs, let's do it\") — split into two companion documents: **PROJECT-STATE-OF-NATION.md** (~7.5pp; what the system IS — two-user architecture, gateway, plugins, skills, sandbox, memory subsystem, config layout, 9-agent roster, heartbeat/coordination model, external dependency map, glossary) and **PROJECT-RUNBOOK.md** (~7.5pp; what to DO — SecretRef chain, per-credential inventory, rotation procedure, op CLI hygiene, F45 gateway restoration ceremony, token/gog/memory/Telegram recovery procedures, config-drift handling, autonomous-vs-escalate boundary, quick-reference card, duplicated glossary). ### S5 — Disaster-recovery dry-run (untested-recovery-path mitigation)
- **What it is:** All credentials backed up to 1Password vault `OpenClaw`. Calendar-backup pipeline produces daily JSON snapshots. Phase C ICS baseline (30 Apr 2026) in 1Password. **But: nobody has ever rebuilt OpenClaw from these backups.** The recovery procedure is implicit, not tested. If the Mini's SSD dies tomorrow, the actual restore path has unknown gaps (which 1Password Notes need restoring in what order? Does the gog OAuth client_secret get re-installed via `gog auth credentials` or by manual placement at file path? Does the gateway plist need re-authoring or is it backed up somewhere? Are there file modes / ownership requirements that scp doesn't preserve?).
- **Mitigation:** at end of 6c (when all 4 agents are operational), do a disaster-recovery dry-run on a different machine: install Homebrew → install OpenClaw → restore .env from 1Password → restore credentials from 1Password (gog client_secret, calendar-backup-token, telegram bot tokens, allowFrom, etc.) → recreate gateway LaunchAgent → run sanity-batch verifications → confirm one bot end-to-end via Telegram. ~3-4 hours; would expose gaps in the recovery path before they bite operationally. **Output: a `DISASTER-RECOVERY-RUNBOOK.md` capturing the empirically-validated restore steps in order.**
- **Target:** post-6c, before extended out-of-pocket periods (vacations, travel). Could fold into the same week as the state-of-nation doc as a "project hardening" pair-session.
- **Owner:** Peter (executes the dry-run; physical/logical complexity makes this human-in-loop work). CoS once operational tracks the post-6c target date + drafts pre-flight checklist (which Notes to retrieve from 1Password, what order to restore, what verification anchors to expect); Peter executes the dry-run on a different machine; Peter authors the resulting `DISASTER-RECOVERY-RUNBOOK.md`. Post-runbook, CoS maintains it as living document — updates entries when underlying credentials or paths change per any S-item or M-item execution.
- **Status:** OPEN — captured at 6a.20 close as strategic risk B. Sustained as standing future work; not blocking any specific session. **6a.32 (A-3):** posture improved — Stage-4.8 vault→gdrive + Stage-5 1Password→encrypted-local mean offsite backups now exist. Full cross-hardware DR dry-run unchanged in scope (post-6c).
- **6a.27 update — operator reboot event dispositioned + restart/recovery procedure authored (S5-adjacent partial mitigation):** During 6a.27 pre-flight, host showed `kern.boottime` Sun 17 May 2026 10:56:56 BST, uptime ~8 min. **Disposition: closed-benign, operator-initiated** — Peter rebooted deliberately to verify the gateway survives restart. Not a crash, not F-class, not state drift. **Durable learning (the empirically-confirmed fact):** the gateway is a `KeepAlive` LaunchAgent (`ai.openclaw.gateway`, plist 2309 / mtime 4 May 22:11 unchanged) and **auto-recovers from a full reboot with no manual action** — confirmed this event: new PID 906 (prior 61289 retired by reboot; respawn is inside the opener's allowed envelope), `healthz:200`, `OPENCLAW_SERVICE_VERSION=2026.4.22`, `GOG_KEYRING_BACKEND=file` present. Manual fallbacks (if auto-recovery ever fails) captured in `PROJECT-RUNBOOK.md` — **runbook provided later in 6a.27 and the procedure was MERGED into §2.1 as the "Post-reboot recovery (expected path)" subsection + a §2.0 symptom-map row; the earlier standalone `PROJECT-RUNBOOK-restart-recovery-INSERT.md` is SUPERSEDED by that merge.** This is a *partial* S5 mitigation (codifies the reboot-recovery path specifically); S5 stays OPEN — the full cross-hardware DR dry-run + `DISASTER-RECOVERY-RUNBOOK.md` (§4.11) is unchanged in scope and the restart section folds into it at S5 execution. **Cross-ref — credential exposure (linked, same pre-flight paste):** `env | grep GOG_KEYRING_` echoed `GOG_KEYRING_PASSWORD` in full into the 6a.27 transcript. **Rotation EVALUATED and DEFERRED at 6a.27 by explicit Peter decision** (prioritise agent build over rotation; accepted-risk interim — NOT performed this session). Logged as standing remediation **F59** (full rotate-when-convenient procedure + interim handling there). ### S6 — Architecture template Part 5 reconcile against 2026.4.22 live schema (added 2026-05-04 at Session 6a.21 close)
- **What it is:** MASTER-ARCHITECTURE-v5-OPTIMIZED.md Part 5 (lines 1072-1187) defines the canonical openclaw.json template. Multiple paths in template are obsolete vs 2026.4.22 live schema, surfaced empirically at 6a.21: (i) `tools.web.search.apiKey` rejected at commit-time validation with "moved to plugins.entries.<plugin>.config.webSearch" — Brave config now lives at plugin-resident path; (ii) `${BRAVE_API_KEY}` env-interpolation syntax superseded by SecretRef builder shape (`--ref-provider/--ref-source/--ref-id` with file-source / json-mode / JSON-pointer id) — old `${VAR}` syntax is template-vintage, current canonical is SecretRef object via `secrets.providers.default` registration; (iii) `models.fallback: "openai/gpt-4o"` (singular string) superseded by `openclaw models fallbacks add <model>` managed verb (plural list, lives outside `models` top-level branch in JSON, accessible via `models status`); (iv) `${OPENCLAW_GATEWAY_TOKEN}` for gateway token superseded by inline literal in live config (no env-resolution observed). Other template paths likely have similar drift but not yet empirically tested at 6a.21 (e.g., `tools.browser.maxConcurrent`, channels schema, agents.defaults memory configs). **Implication:** future sessions touching template paths in 6a.22 cluster B (cron + browser concurrency) and 6a.23 cluster C (Obsidian + Granola) and 6b PA build (per-agent workspace + auth-profiles) all need empirical verification per per-version flag-semantics drift discipline. Cumulative cost of per-session per-path verification adds up.
- **Mitigation:** post-6c (after all 4 agents operational + Phase G workspace setup landed) one-shot reconciliation pass: walk template Part 5 from line 1072 through 1187 + map each path to current live `openclaw config schema` output + flag every divergence. Output: revised `MASTER-ARCHITECTURE-v5.1.md` (or v6.md) with Part 5 reflecting 2026.4.22 reality. ~2-3 hours of focused architecture-grep work + comparison + rewriting. Ideally folded into the same week as S4 state-of-nation doc + S5 disaster-recovery dry-run as a "project hardening" pair-session.
- **Target:** post-6c, alongside S4 + S5. Or sooner if cumulative per-session reconciliation cost becomes painful — could fold into 6a.24 (memory verification session, otherwise lightweight) as opportunistic side-work.
- **Owner:** Peter (architectural reconciliation requires holistic understanding of intent vs current schema; not delegatable to CoS until CoS is operational + has seen this pattern). Once 6c lands and CoS workspace authored, ownership transfers to Andreas/CoS per D19 audit-trail responsibility — CoS maintains template currency as part of project-state-of-nation document upkeep (extension of S4).
- **6a.25 update — two verification-methodology sub-facts (not template-path obsolescence, but anchor-methodology drift worth locking):** **(i) agents.list sub-hash methodology normalised.** 6a.25 Stage 1 emitted `agents_sha12=04e7c53d3194` vs the locked anchor `2c1a43c2117a`. Full-file sha12 (`de5d880fd373`) + byte-size (7285) matched 6a.24 close EXACTLY → agents.list content byte-identical; the sub-hash divergence is a serialization-methodology difference (6a.25 computed via `json.dumps(agents, sort_keys=True)`; the historical anchor used a different convention, never formally captured). **Resolution: lock `04e7c53d3194` as the canonical agents.list sub-hash going forward, computed via `json.dumps(agents, sort_keys=True)`.** Full-file sha12 remains the dispositive anchor; the sub-hash is a convenience check. Pattern lesson: convenience sub-anchors must have their computation method captured at lock time, or they generate false-drift signals across instances. **(ii) SecretRef structural check retired as unreliable.** 6a.25 Stage 1 `brave_apiKey_is_secretRef` / `openai_apiKey_is_secretRef` checks returned False, but full-file sha12 was unchanged → content byte-identical to 6a.24 close where SecretRef was empirically intact (per S4.7/S4.9 6a.21 closures). The check's structural assumption (literal `secretRef` key inside an `apiKey` dict) does not match the 2026.4.22 schema shape (SecretRefs resolve via `secrets.providers.default` → `secrets.json`, structure is `{source, provider, id}` not `{secretRef: …}`). **Do not rely on this boolean check.** If SecretRef intactness ever needs direct verification, dump the actual block (`jq '.plugins.entries.brave.config, .models.providers.openai'`) and inspect shape, or trust `openclaw secrets audit unresolved=0` as the canonical signal (per F54 6a.23 standing rule). These two sub-facts are methodology hygiene, not new obsolete template paths — S6's instance count stays at three (`tools.web.search.apiKey` / `${VAR}` interpolation / `tools.browser.maxConcurrent`).
- **6a.23 update — S6 third obsolescence instance**: at 6a.23 Stage 4 architecture-grep, `tools.browser.maxConcurrent` (architecture template Part 5 line 1091) confirmed obsolete in 2026.4.22 — `tools.browser` does not exist as a schema path (`tools.properties` keys are `agentToAgent, allow, alsoAllow, byProvider, deny, elevated, exec, experimental, fs, links, loopDetection, media, message, profile, sandbox, sessions, sessions_spawn, subagents, web` — no `browser`); top-level `browser.maxConcurrent` does not exist (`browser.properties` has 16 keys covering CDP / profile / executable settings, none for concurrency); `plugins.entries.browser.config.properties` is empty (no schema for plugin-resident browser config in 2026.4.22). The browser concurrency knob has been retired entirely. Closest semantic equivalent surfaced is `agents.defaults.maxConcurrent` (integer, no description in schema, no default, no minimum, max effectively unbounded at 2^53-1) — undocumented and ambiguous semantic intent (could be tool-invocation concurrency, sub-agent spawn cap, session count, or other). **Stage 5.C dropped at 6a.23**; concurrency knob restoration deferred indefinitely (no operational pressure with no agents running yet). **Three S6 instances now**: (1) `tools.web.search.apiKey` migration to `plugins.entries.brave.config.webSearch.apiKey` (6a.21 S4.7); (2) `${VAR}` env-interpolation supersession by SecretRef builder shape (6a.21); (3) **`tools.browser.maxConcurrent` retirement entirely with no clean port** (6a.23). Cumulative S6 reconciliation cost is rising — three confirmed obsolete paths after only two cluster-B sessions empirically tested. Recommend scheduling the post-6c hygiene pass sooner (consider folding into 6a.24 Cluster C if Obsidian/Granola surfaces additional template drift, OR scheduling between 6a.25 and Phase G as standalone S6 reconciliation session). **6a.27 update — FOUR S6 instances now**: (4) **`memorySearch.provider:"local"` documented-but-unimplemented** — 2026.4.22 `config schema` `provider` description explicitly lists `"local"` as valid, but the runtime adapter registry rejects it: `memory status --deep` hard-throws `Error: Unknown memory embedding provider: local` at `getAdapter`. Inverse failure mode of (1)-(3): not a renamed/retired path but a SHIPPED-SCHEMA capability with NO runtime adapter. Architecture `agents.defaults.memorySearch.provider:"local"` is obsolete-in-practice on 2026.4.22. Empirically proven at 6a.27 Stage 3a (write landed+validated, runtime rejected on restart); D22 → OpenAI as a result. **Generalised lesson: treat any schema-sourced capability as UNPROVEN until exercised at runtime** — schema-validity (even `config validate` rc=0) does NOT imply runtime implementation. Four confirmed S6 instances; post-6c hygiene pass still outstanding. **Sub-fact for closure**: cron jobs in 2026.4.22 are stored at `~/.openclaw/cron/jobs.json` (per `openclaw cron status` output `storePath: /Users/openclaw/.openclaw/cron/jobs.json`) — outside openclaw.json. Stage 5.A (deferred) anchor capture pattern would extend to `~/.openclaw/cron/jobs.json` at agent-build-time when cron entries land per-agent.

### S7 — Agent Documentation System per architecture §3.13 mandate (operational expansion; added 2026-05-05 at Session 6a.23 close)
- **What it is:** Master architecture §3.13 mandates a two-layer documentation system (per-agent docs + shared knowledge base) with CoS as documentation owner, version control, central storage, and shareability with friends/collaborators/advisors. §3.13 establishes the architectural mandate but is light on operational detail — what "always up-to-date" means in practice, how doc currency is enforced, how docs are searched/discovered/onboarded, what quality standards govern content, how confidentiality tiers map to access control, how external-facing materials are managed, and how the system integrates with existing session artifacts (DEVIATIONS-LOG, closure docs, master architecture). S7 captures the world-class operational scope required to translate §3.13's architectural mandate into a maintainable, discoverable, defensible documentation system meeting the same quality bar as the rest of the build. Surfaced as previously-implicit Phase 1 deliverable made explicit at 6a.23 close per Peter's directive ("complete and detailed, production-grade documentation for our entire openclaw architecture").
- **Scope (10 operational sub-items expanding §3.13):**
  - **(1) Per-agent documentation** — implicit-safe scope, lands at 6b/6c/6d workspace authoring sessions naturally: SOUL.md (identity, persona, voice), AGENTS.md (standing orders, autonomy level, capabilities, behaviour change history), DECISIONS.md (every persona/policy/scope decision logged with date + rationale), TOOLS.md (tool allow/deny list with justification per tool), HEARTBEAT.md (cadence rules for autonomous-execution agents), USER.md (per-agent reference into Peter's context). All version-controlled; commit history is the change history. Each agent updates own per-agent docs; CoS audits currency.
  - **(2) Shared knowledge base** — explicit scaffolding required, ~12-15 documents covering: security architecture and policies (mirrors §4.1 + extracted F-row resolutions); memory system design and maintenance procedures (§3.1); inter-agent coordination protocols (§3.8); heartbeat and cron configurations (per-agent specs + system-level cron registry); inbox management workflows (PA + ProA inbox conventions, triage rules); calendar management conventions (PA + ProA + CoS calendar protocols); file architecture and naming conventions; CRM schema and pipeline definitions (SDR + Travel + Finance scope); disaster recovery runbooks (extracted from §4.11); deployment runbooks (Phase 0 sequence + agent-build sequence + **`skills-manifest.md` per §4.1 #6 + §4.11 + `cron-manifest.md` per §4.11**, both extracted from current Config repo state); per-skill install steps); credential rotation procedures (extracted from F25 lineage + per-credential resolution paths); F-row + D-row + S-row catalogue (mirror of DEVIATIONS-LOG indexed for navigation); architecture-template Part 5 reconciliation (S6 closure deliverable); glossary (terms, acronyms, agent names + roles); index/sitemap for navigation; agent ingestion manifests (per-Claude-session reading-order scripts).
  - **(3) Storage-location decision (Phase G scope):** candidates Notion / Confluence / dedicated GitHub repo / Obsidian vault subfolder / Workspace Drive folder. Decision factors: (a) accessibility from Mini SSH context for CoS-owned auto-update workflows, (b) multi-device readability for Peter, (c) shareability with external collaborators, (d) version-control native vs bolted-on, (e) search quality, (f) offline access, (g) cost. Decision deferred to Phase G when Obsidian is operational post-Cluster-C and can be empirically evaluated as a candidate; Workspace Drive becomes available post-Internal-flip. Default lean if no clear winner: dedicated GitHub repo `pfedchen-openclaw/openclaw-docs` (private; mirrors agent workspace repo pattern; git-native versioning; shareable via collaborator invite; markdown-native; ingest-friendly for Claude sessions). Sub-decision: confidentiality tiers (public / internal / restricted) implemented via separate repos OR access-controlled subdirectories OR git-crypt-encrypted files.
  - **(4) CoS doc-currency duties (6c CoS workspace authoring scope):** embed in CoS AGENTS.md as standing orders parallel to the 11 Operating System Ownership bullets. Concrete duties: (a) weekly doc-staleness audit producing report; (b) post-execution doc-update prompt for any M-item / S-item / D-row / F-row resolution; (c) per-agent persona-drift detection (compare current SOUL.md vs commit-3-months-ago to surface unintended drift); (d) cross-reference integrity check (link rot detection); (e) public-facing doc curation gate (CoS reviews before any external share); (f) freshness signal enforcement (every doc has last-reviewed timestamp; CoS escalates anything >90 days). Quality bar enforcement: every doc must have frontmatter (title, owner, audience, last-reviewed, related-docs); every doc declares scope upfront; every doc has linked verification or test where applicable. CoS produces monthly doc-system health report **including Anthropic spend tracking** (per §4.1 #11 $1,000/month soft ceiling): per-agent token consumption + per-agent dollar spend + heartbeat efficiency metrics + month-over-month trend + alert threshold breach summary. PA owns standing-order cost-optimization duties (per §4.1 #11 "PA has access to manage and optimise costs"); CoS aggregates and reports.
  - **(5) Documentation governance (style + quality + lifecycle):** **Style guide** — voice/tone consistency (Paul Graham clarity per USER-VOICE-GUIDE; no fluff; concrete > abstract); markdown conventions (headings, code blocks, tables); cross-reference format. **Quality checklist** — clarity (intelligent operator with zero context can follow); completeness (no dangling refs or undefined terms); accuracy (verified against current state, not historical); freshness (last-reviewed within 90 days); discoverability (linked from index). **Doc-creation triggers** — every D-row needs a knowledge-base entry; every F-row resolution needs a procedure doc; every M-item needs a runbook; every S-item closure produces durable doc; per-agent persona changes auto-update SOUL.md commit history. **Doc-deletion process** — docs marked obsolete via frontmatter `status: archived` rather than deleted; CoS produces quarterly archive review; physical deletion only for clear-mistakes or supersession (with redirect note). **Versioning** — git-native; per-doc semver in frontmatter for major rewrites (1.0.0 → 2.0.0 if scope changes); commit message convention (`docs(security): rotate AC-7 credentials procedure`). **Review process** — CoS reviews changes touching shared knowledge base; per-agent docs trust-based with CoS audit; Peter reviews any change to security architecture or credential rotation procedures.
  - **(6) Confidentiality tiers (parallel to USER.md / USER-CONTEXT-RESTRICTED.md split):** **Public tier** — shareable with friends/collaborators/advisors per §3.13; covers system architecture overview, agent roles, technology stack; no PII, no specific contacts, no credentials, no business specifics. **Internal tier** — operator-readable; full system context including specific configurations, agent persona details, calendar/email conventions; no credentials, no PII. **Restricted tier** — credential rotation procedures, security architecture details, disaster-recovery secrets, PII-touching workflows; access limited to Peter + agents whitelisted per §3.11 (PA / Sophie / Finance / Travel). **Implementation** — separate repos OR access-controlled subdirectories OR git-crypt-encrypted files; decision at Phase G alongside storage location. **Tier markers** — every doc has frontmatter `tier: public|internal|restricted`; CoS enforces tier compliance pre-publication.
  - **(7) External-facing materials (post-shared-knowledge-base scope):** **Public-tier curation** — CoS produces "OpenClaw — what it is and how it works" overview suitable for sharing; written for intelligent reader with no context. **Anonymisation rules** — replace specific contacts with generic placeholders; redact business specifics; keep architecture and technology specifics (these are the interesting parts for external readers). **Marketing copy** — separate from technical reference; lighter weight; aimed at "should I do this for my own life?" question. **Update cadence** — lighter than internal docs; quarterly review unless system architecture changes.
  - **(8) Integration with existing session artifacts:** DEVIATIONS-LOG remains canonical authority for D-rows / F-rows / S-rows / M-items; knowledge base references but never duplicates (pointer-style references per Lesson #9 standing rule from 6a.23). Closure docs remain session-scoped working artifacts; knowledge base distills durable findings post-session via CoS curation. Master architecture remains locked baseline; knowledge base captures empirical post-build state with explicit deltas-from-spec markers. **Migration story** — at Phase 1 build completion, CoS produces "DEVIATIONS-LOG → knowledge-base distillation pass" extracting every closed F-row into procedure doc, every D-row into decisions doc, every S-row closure into runbook. Session opener docs reference knowledge base as state-of-build context (replaces the current closure-doc-attachment pattern post-Phase-1).
  - **(9) Documentation disaster recovery:** local mirror at `~/.openclaw/docs-mirror/` updated via cron (5-minute frequency for active edits; daily full sync). Off-site backup: knowledge-base repo replicated to Workspace Drive nightly per §4.11 disaster recovery patterns. Storage-host outage protocol: CoS uses local mirror for read; queues writes; flushes when storage returns. Repo corruption recovery: full restore from Drive backup; <30 min target.
  - **(10) Search and discoverability:** master index/sitemap doc auto-generated from frontmatter (last build timestamp visible). Tag-based navigation (every doc has frontmatter tags). **Full-text search** — GitHub native (if dedicated repo); Obsidian's vault search (if Obsidian); Notion native (if Notion). **Per-Claude-session ingestion manifests** — pre-curated reading orders for common tasks ("rebuild PA agent" → load these docs in this order; "investigate F-row pattern" → load these docs).
- **Sequencing:** **6c CoS workspace authoring** — CoS doc-currency duties embedded in CoS AGENTS.md (Item 4); confidentiality tier framework finalised (Item 6 sub-decision). **Phase G (6a.26 combined Screen Sharing session per 4-session 6a-tier plan)** — storage location locked (Item 3); confidentiality-tier implementation chosen. **Post-6d dedicated documentation mini-session** — shared knowledge base initial scaffolding (Item 2); style guide + governance protocols authored (Item 5); ingestion manifests (Item 10); ~4-6 hours; **also includes 1Password Note `w2fw6s5naommpamza5qbeltrcu` cleanup per Lesson #9 standing rule (rewrite as pointer-style Note referencing canonical S7 knowledge base entries; OR delete entirely if F55 launchd LaunchAgents have by then been bootstrapped and the plist designs are no longer useful)**. **Post-shared-knowledge-base** — external-facing materials curation (Item 7); ~2 hours. **Ongoing** — CoS-owned currency maintenance per Item 4 standing orders.
- **Relationship to other items:** **S4** (bus-factor 5-page operator onramp) becomes a section inside S7's shared knowledge base once both exist; S4 can land standalone earlier in 6a-tier (preserves bus-factor mitigation immediately) and gets subsumed into knowledge base post-S7-storage-decision. **D19** (maintenance-cadence-ownership) — CoS doc-currency duties extend D19's audit-trail responsibility; explicit alignment in CoS AGENTS.md. **Master architecture §3.13** — S7 is the operational expansion of §3.13's architectural mandate; if architecture v6 ships, S7 folds into a revised §3.13 (this would be a separate D-row decision; not pursuing now). **Master architecture §4.11** (disaster recovery) — docs-DR (Item 9) extends §4.11 patterns. **F-row catalogue** sub-item of shared knowledge base (Item 2) provides searchable index over DEVIATIONS-LOG for future-Claude sessions. **Lesson #9 from 6a.23** (1Password Notes pointer-style default) — S7 closure handles the existing redundant Note explicitly. **S8/S9/S10/S11/M7 (audit-revealed at 6a.23 close)** — S7 knowledge base serves as documentation home for: S8 pre-6b gate validation procedures (so future agent-build sessions and post-launch re-validations have a runnable gate procedure); S9 system-wide automation runbooks (auto-update validation flow, secret-scanning before push, workspace self-mod monitoring, session retention archive, WhatsApp health check, weekly backup ceremony, memory-pressure monitoring); S10 Soveren.io migration phase tracking + reminder cadence; S11 inter-agent rate limiting + loop protection design specs; M7 security recurring hygiene cycle runbooks (CVE tracker, weekly npm outdated, monthly key rotation, OAuth scope verify, skills review, MEMORY.md review, stolen device protocol). S7 Item 4 doc-currency duties enforce freshness across all five companion structural rows; S7 Item 4 monthly health report aggregates S9 sub-item (7) memory-pressure samples + M7 cadence-cycle completion + Anthropic spend tracking into single Peter-facing summary.
