### S9 — System-wide automation + lifecycle workflows not covered by D21 (added 2026-05-05 at Session 6a.23 close)
- **What it is:** Architecture §3.7 cron jobs schedule + §4.1 security hardening + §4.10 Docker monitoring + §4.11 disaster recovery specify multiple system-wide automation + lifecycle workflows. **D21 captures the cron-architecture deferral broadly** (openclaw cron + macOS crontab → launchd LaunchAgents Screen Sharing mini-session). **D21's deferral does NOT explicitly cover** the SOPHISTICATED workflow design + secret-scanning + lifecycle-policy + Week-1-monitoring components for several specific automation tasks. S9 captures these workflow-design deliverables explicitly.
- **Scope (7 sub-items):**
  - **(1) Sunday 4am OpenClaw auto-update + validation flow + auto-rollback** per §3.7. Workflow: (i) `openclaw backup create` first as restoration anchor; (ii) `openclaw update` apply; (iii) gateway restart; (iv) `openclaw doctor` validation; (v) `openclaw security audit --deep` validation; (vi) test message to CoS + verify response within timeout; (vii) if any validation step fails, auto-rollback from pre-update backup + alert Peter via Telegram URGENT; (viii) log validation results regardless; (ix) Telegram report to Peter showing what was updated, validation status, any errors. **Sunday timing chosen** so Peter has time to monitor/fix if rollback fires. Weekday: check-only mode (`openclaw update --check`) reports via Telegram without applying. **Architectural complexity**: 9-step workflow with conditional branching; needs explicit design + scripting; subsumes M4 (OpenClaw updates) quarterly evaluation cadence into automated weekly cycle.
  - **(2) Daily 4am workspace git auto-push + secret scanning before push** per §3.7 + step 15 + VelvetShark Use Case 3. Workflow: (i) for each agent's workspace at `~/.openclaw/workspace-<agentId>/`, scan for leaked secrets via regex/entropy patterns (API keys, OAuth tokens, card numbers, passwords); (ii) replace any matches with placeholders + log redactions; (iii) `git add -A && git commit -m "daily auto-snapshot $(date +%Y-%m-%d)"`; (iv) `git push origin main`; (v) verify push success + log; (vi) if scan finds secrets, alert Peter URGENT (means secrets ended up in workspace files which is a leak). **Step 15 currently shows `[ ]` deferred per D21**; S9 sub-item (2) defines the SECRET-SCANNING component explicitly so it doesn't get lost in step 15 implementation.
  - **(3) Hourly workspace self-modification monitoring** per §4.1 #18. Workflow: every hour, check `git status` across all 9 agent workspaces; if SOUL.md / AGENTS.md / DECISIONS.md / TOOLS.md / HEARTBEAT.md show uncommitted changes, alert Peter via Telegram URGENT (means an agent or process modified its own persona files outside the version-control discipline). **Cadence note**: hourly is aggressive; consider whether 15-minute cadence catches drift faster vs hourly batches better; Peter to confirm at 6c CoS build.
  - **(4) Session retention 90-day lifecycle + Google Drive archive** per §4.1 #19. Workflow: nightly cron scans `~/.openclaw/agents/<agentId>/sessions/` directories; identifies session files older than 90 days; archives them to Google Drive (per-agent subfolder); after Drive upload verified, prunes from local. **Cadence**: nightly part of 11pm consolidation OR separate weekly cron. Implementation requires gog OAuth scope to write to Drive (`drive.file`) — out of current OAuth grants (current scope is gmail.modify + calendar.events); **scope expansion needed**.
  - **(5) WhatsApp session health check in meta-monitoring** per §3.7 + §4.1 #10. Workflow: every 2 hours, the meta-monitoring cron (deferred per D21) checks Sophie's WhatsApp session state; if disconnected/expired, alert Peter URGENT. **Currently captured under D21's general meta-monitoring deferral** but the WhatsApp-specific health-check component was omitted in D21's scope statement; S9 makes it explicit so it doesn't get lost. **Sequencing**: only applies post-Sophie-WhatsApp-channel-active (Phase 3 / Month 2+ per D4 — Sophie starts in Telegram for Day 1).
  - **(6) `openclaw backup create` weekly cron + Google Drive upload** per §4.11. Workflow: weekly cron runs `openclaw backup create` (auth-profiles + session history); uploads tarball to Google Drive `OpenClaw-Backups/` folder; rotates retention (keep 12 weekly snapshots = ~3 months of weekly granularity). Same Drive scope dependency as sub-item (4).
  - **(7) 8am window memory_pressure monitoring** per §4.10 + Part 9 item 34. **Week 1 explicit monitoring**: run `memory_pressure` or Activity Monitor during 8am morning briefing window (when CoS scans all digests + email while PA + ProA run heartbeats simultaneously — risk of swap on 16GB Mini). If "Warning" or "Critical" memory pressure or swap activity appears, action plan: (a) reduce Docker memory limit 6GB → 4GB; (b) reduce browser concurrency 3 → 2; (c) if still swapping, consider offloading browser-heavy agents to cloud VM. **Ongoing post-Week-1 monitoring**: monthly sample during 8am window logged to CoS health report (per S7 Item 4).
- **Sequencing:** **6a.26 combined Screen Sharing session** lands F55 launchd LaunchAgents infrastructure that enables sub-items (1), (2), (3), (5), (6) — those depend on launchd LaunchAgents being bootstrapped. Sub-items (2), (4), (6) require Drive-write OAuth scope expansion which lands at the same 6a.26 session (combined with Phase G Workspace setup; saves one Screen Sharing trip per 4-session 6a-tier plan finalised at 6a.23 close). Sub-item (7) Week 1 memory_pressure monitoring lands at 6b PA build session opening (post-Marie-launch). Sub-item (5) WhatsApp health lands at Sophie WhatsApp channel migration (Phase 3 / Month 2+).
- **Owner:** Peter through 6c (workflow design + script authoring + cron registration). CoS at 6c+ for ongoing monitoring + alert escalation + monthly health report (S7 Item 4 + S12 expansion).
- **Status:** OPEN — 7 sub-items captured at 6a.23 close as audit-revealed system-wide automation gaps not in D21's scope.
- **Closes when:** each sub-item's specific workflow is implemented + operational + tested with at least one full successful cycle. S9 stays OPEN until all 7 sub-items resolved.

### S10 — Soveren.io email sunset multi-month migration plan (added 2026-05-05 at Session 6a.23 close)
- **What it is:** Architecture §3.12 Soveren.io email sunset plan specifies a multi-month migration with ProA + PA jointly owning execution. **Cross-cutting concern that spans 6c ProA build + 6b PA build + 8+ months of agent-driven execution** — without explicit tracking, risk that Month 1-2 dual monitoring lands in ProA AGENTS.md but Month 3-4 audit work + Month 5-6 disconnect + Month 8+ full removal get lost in attention to per-agent persona work.
- **Scope (4 phases per §3.12):**
  - **(1) Month 1-2 dual monitoring** — ProA monitors both @hylean.com (when live) and @soveren.io. Auto-redirect routine inquiries from @soveren.io to @hylean.com (or pfedchen@gmail.com if @hylean.com not yet live per Phase 1 step 33 fallback). Standing orders embed in ProA AGENTS.md at 6c authoring. **Dependencies**: @hylean.com Workspace operational (Phase G) + ProA OAuth registered against @soveren.io (currently deferred per E2 plan-doc; lands at 6c).
  - **(2) Month 3-4 audit + migration** — PA + ProA jointly audit all subscriptions, accounts, and credentials linked to @soveren.io. Migrate everything to @hylean.com or pfedchen@gmail.com as appropriate. **No active sending from @soveren.io in this phase**. Standing orders embed in PA + ProA AGENTS.md. Procedural details: scan email history for service-registration confirmations; per service, identify migration target; execute migration (manual web-UI for most services); verify migration successful; mark service in tracker; report progress weekly.
  - **(3) Month 5-6 (or when Soveren legal entity closes) auto-forward** — @soveren.io set to auto-forward to pfedchen@gmail.com. **No agent monitoring at this phase**. Trigger: Soveren legal entity closure OR end-of-Month-6 schedule, whichever comes first.
  - **(4) Month 8+ full disconnect** — Auto-forward maintained for 3 additional months (Month 8-11), then removed. @soveren.io domain DNS configuration retired or domain itself released. Final closure ceremony.
- **Sequencing:** Phase (1) starts at 6c ProA build; Phase (2) kicks in at Month 3 (~end July 2026 if 6c lands May 2026); Phase (3) at Month 5 (~end September 2026); Phase (4) at Month 8 (~end December 2026). **Calendar reminder advisable** for Phase (2) kickoff + Phase (3) trigger + Phase (4) trigger; CoS owns the calendar reminders post-6c per S7 Item 4 doc-currency duties + M-row cadence pattern.
- **Owner:** Peter for legal-entity-closure decisions. PA + ProA for execution at agent layer. CoS for cadence + reminder + audit trail.
- **Status:** OPEN — captured at 6a.23 close as cross-cutting multi-month plan made explicit per audit findings.
- **Closes when:** Phase (4) fully executes — auto-forward removed, @soveren.io domain decision finalised, all linked services migrated, no active monitoring or forwarding.

### S11 — Inter-agent rate limiting + loop protection design (added 2026-05-05 at Session 6a.23 close)
- **What it is:** Architecture §3.8 specifies rate + loop protection: "If any two agents exchange more than 10 messages in one hour, pause exchange and alert Peter via CoS." Part 9 item 32 expands: "simple hard rate limits are insufficient, need pattern-based detection." **Implementation undesigned** — needs explicit engineering work covering: where the counter lives, how patterns are detected, circuit-breaker behavior, recovery flow.
- **Design questions (CoS scope at 6c):**
  - **(a) Counter location**: gateway-level (every `sessions_send` invocation increments inter-agent counter) vs CoS-monitored (CoS scans all daily digests + sessions logs for inter-agent exchanges; more flexible but slower detection) vs hybrid (gateway hard counter + CoS pattern detection).
  - **(b) Pattern-based detection vs hard rate limit**: per Part 9 item 32, hard rate limits insufficient. Patterns to detect: ping-pong (A→B→A→B→A→B...); wide-fanout (A→{B,C,D,E,F}); recursive (A→B causes B→C causes C→A); rapid-burst (5 msgs in 60s vs 5 msgs in 60min). Each pattern needs threshold + detection logic.
  - **(c) Circuit-breaker behavior**: when threshold breached, pause exchange how? gateway-level rejection of `sessions_send` with error to caller? agent-level acknowledgment but queue rather than execute? Affects how requesting agent recovers.
  - **(d) Peter's notification path**: CoS sends Telegram URGENT with details: which agents, message count, pattern type detected, recent message summaries. Includes 'pause/resume' button for Peter to clear circuit breaker.
  - **(e) Recovery flow**: how does paused exchange resume? Manual Peter approval? Automatic decay (counter drops below threshold)? Manual override required + logged in DECISIONS.md?
  - **(f) False-positive handling**: legitimate high-volume exchanges (e.g., Sophie pings PA 12 times in an hour to coordinate Leo schedule changes) shouldn't trigger pause. Whitelist patterns or trusted-context flags?
- **Sequencing:** Design lands at 6c CoS workspace authoring as part of CoS's Operating System Ownership remit (parallel to the 11 ownership bullets per §2.5 CoS profile). Implementation may need cross-agent coordination at 6d (each agent's `sessions_send` call site needs awareness of circuit-breaker state). Empirical tuning post-launch (false-positive rates, threshold calibration).
- **Owner:** CoS owns design + implementation + tuning per §2.5 Operating System Ownership remit. Peter approves design at 6c build review.
- **Status:** OPEN — captured at 6a.23 close as undesigned implementation per Part 9 item 32 explicit flag.
- **Closes when:** Design approved + implemented + tested with at least one synthetic threshold-breach scenario showing correct circuit-breaker behavior + Peter's notification + recovery flow.
## Maintenance cadence + update discipline

_Items that are NOT point-in-time mitigations (those are Strategic Risks above) but recurring maintenance disciplines. The framework: identify each external software dependency the project relies on, spec a cadence for evaluating it, and a treatment pattern when it does need updating. Without explicit discipline here, dependencies silently age into operational risk over months. Added 2026-05-03 at 6a.20 close after Peter's "old libraries / cleanup" review._

### M1 — Python user-site dependencies (24 google-* transitive deps from 6a.20)
- **What:** `google-api-python-client`, `google-auth`, `google-auth-oauthlib`, `cryptography`, `urllib3`, `requests`, plus 18 transitive deps installed at `~/Library/Python/3.9/lib/python/site-packages/` per 6a.20 Phase B. Powers Phase D calendar-backup pipeline.
- **Risk if neglected:** library 2.x → 3.x breaking changes; deprecated Google API endpoints; security CVEs in older versions; transitive dep version hell. Most acutely: intersection with D18 (Python 3.9 EOL) means when libraries drop 3.9 support, next `pip install --upgrade` either fails or installs versions that don't import.
- **Cadence:** quarterly evaluation. Each quarter: `pip3 list --outdated --user` to see what's drifted; `pip3 install --user --upgrade google-api-python-client google-auth google-auth-oauthlib` to update primary deps (transitives follow); run `bash ~/.openclaw/scripts/calendar-backup.py` interactively to smoke-test; if green, 1Password-update token note (refresh token may have rotated); if red, pin to last-working version + characterise + defer to dedicated session.
- **Treatment of major version bumps:** any 2.x → 3.x version jump in primary deps is treated as state-changing ceremony — pin to last 2.x first, verify smoke-test green, then evaluate 3.x compatibility separately.
- **Closure path:** absorbs into D18 migration session naturally — D18 rebuilds user-site under Homebrew python@3.13 with then-current package versions, resetting the cadence clock. After D18, this cadence resumes at the new interpreter.
- **Owner:** Peter through 6c, then transfers to Andreas/CoS per D19. CoS runs the quarterly check (next-due tracking + `pip3 list --outdated --user` reminder + draft of upgrade ceremony shape); Peter executes the actual `pip3 install --user --upgrade ...` ceremony + smoke-test. Audit trail of each cycle's outcome (what versions pinned, what versions upgraded) maintained by CoS in M1's row updates.
- **Status:** ACTIVE — first cadence cycle due ~August 2026 (3 months from 6a.20). Calendar reminder advisable.

### M2 — gogcli updates (Brew formula)
- **What:** gogcli ships via Homebrew; `brew upgrade gogcli` will offer 0.14.1+ when published. Currently at 0.14.0 per locked reference.
- **Risk if neglected:** behind on security patches; behind on bug fixes (F46 might close in upstream 0.15.x; F47 might be addressed); but ALSO: blind `brew upgrade gogcli` is NOT free per F48 evidence — version transitions can cause calendar-service auth-registry schema drift requiring re-grant ceremony.
- **Cadence:** evaluate on `brew update` notification (not on a calendar). When brew shows gogcli has updates available: review release notes via `brew log gogcli` or upstream CHANGELOG; identify whether release affects calendar-service / auth registry / keyring schema (per F48 + F46 patterns); if schema-touching, treat as state-changing ceremony.
- **Treatment of any gogcli upgrade:** sanity-batch BEFORE upgrade (`gog auth list` + `gog --version` + keyring-file inventory); `brew upgrade gogcli`; sanity-batch AFTER upgrade (same checks); smoke-test calendar + gmail endpoints; if any service shows "no auth" pattern (F48 signature), run E1 OAuth re-grant ceremony. Calendar-backup pipeline uses path (c) Python bypass and is INSENSITIVE to gogcli upgrade — only gog-routed agent operations (PA gmail/calendar via gateway) are affected.
- **Owner:** Peter through 6c, then transfers to Andreas/CoS per D19. CoS monitors `brew outdated` output for gogcli upgrades + reads upstream CHANGELOG when surfaced + flags Peter when release affects calendar-service / auth registry / keyring schema; Peter executes the upgrade ceremony (sanity-batch + brew upgrade + post-verification + re-grant if F48 signature surfaces).
- **Status:** STANDING — no immediate action needed; evaluate on next upgrade availability.

### M3 — macOS major version updates
- **What:** Mac Mini currently on macOS Tahoe (per `arm64_tahoe.bottle` flag in 6a.20 brew output). Apple ships major macOS updates ~yearly.
- **Risk if neglected:** falling behind on security patches; eventual incompatibility with newer Homebrew bottles; eventually an Apple system Python update that may surface different version (could intersect with D18 in unexpected ways). **But major OS updates are NOT free either** — D11 captures FileVault restart behaviour; D15 captured keychain ACL friction; F45 surfaced LaunchAgent unregistration during a keychain ceremony. Major OS updates can break: launchd state + keychain ACLs + Python's bundled libraries + Homebrew's bottle ABI compatibility.
- **Cadence:** evaluate twice yearly (Apple typically WWDC announces in June, ships fall, point-releases through following spring). DON'T install major macOS updates during business-active periods; reserve for dedicated maintenance windows.
- **Treatment of any macOS major version update:** treat as state-changing ceremony with FULL session budget — pre-update sanity batch (entire DEVIATIONS-LOG locked-references list); 1Password backup of all credential files (full filesystem snapshot of `~/.openclaw/credentials/` to a Note); Time Machine snapshot if available; THEN install update; post-update verification batch (same locked-references checked); F45-style gateway restoration if needed; gog re-grant if calendar-service/keyring schema drift surfaces; calendar-backup smoke-test. ~2-3 hour session. Don't update macOS major versions casually.
- **Owner:** Peter through 6c, then transfers to Andreas/CoS per D19 for tracking-and-reminding only. CoS maintains the twice-yearly evaluation cadence + flags Apple WWDC announcements + reminds Peter when next major lands; Peter ALWAYS executes macOS major-version updates (never agent-autonomous; ceremony complexity + risk profile makes this human-only work). Note: macOS major updates can break gateway plist / keychain ACLs / Python's bundled libraries, so post-update F45-style restoration may be required (CoS pre-drafts the restoration ceremony as part of the upgrade-evaluation deliverable).
- **Status:** STANDING — Tahoe is current as of 6a.20; next major likely ~Sept 2026 (Apple's standard cadence). Sequencing implication: don't update macOS during 6a-tier infrastructure or 6b/6c agent build sessions; reserve for after Phase G.

### M4 — OpenClaw updates
- **What:** OpenClaw 4.22 per D1; currently 8 releases ahead of original Phase 0 pin (4.14). Active development; updates ship regularly.
- **Risk if neglected:** falling behind on agent-runtime fixes; behind on plugin compatibility (Active Memory plugin 2026.4.10+ per F3); behind on schema changes that may eventually affect openclaw.json validation. **But OpenClaw upgrades are NOT free either** — F3 Active Memory plugin shipped post-pin; F18 v7 hot-reload classification was empirically derived per-version; openclaw config schema may evolve.
- **Cadence:** evaluate quarterly. Check OpenClaw changelog for: agent runtime changes; openclaw.json schema changes; gateway/plugin/channel layer changes. If changelog shows touching active subsystems (telegram channel, gateway, agents.list, workspace), treat upgrade as state-changing ceremony.
- **Treatment of any OpenClaw upgrade:** sanity-batch BEFORE (full locked-references list — config sha12, agents.list sha12, all 4 bot tokens, gateway state, etc.); read changelog for behavioural changes; 1Password backup of `~/.openclaw/openclaw.json` to a Note; `brew upgrade openclaw` (or wherever the install path is — verify at upgrade time); sanity-batch AFTER (same checks); F18 v7 hot-reload re-classification if config schema touched (some keys may need full gateway restart to take effect post-upgrade); smoke-test all 4 bots if telegram channel layer touched.
- **Closure path:** never closes; standing discipline.
- **Owner:** Peter through 6c, then transfers to Andreas/CoS per D19. CoS monitors OpenClaw release feed + reads changelogs for behavioural changes + flags Peter when changelog touches active subsystems (telegram channel, gateway, agents.list, workspace, plugins); Peter executes the upgrade ceremony with full sanity-batch protocol. Post-upgrade, CoS audits whether F18 v7 hot-reload classification needs re-derivation for any newly-touched config keys + updates DEVIATIONS-LOG accordingly.
- **Status:** STANDING — defer first OpenClaw upgrade evaluation to post-6b PA build (so PA workspace authoring doesn't get destabilised by mid-build runtime changes); thereafter quarterly. **6a.26 update —** `2026.5.12` available (per `update-check.json` `2026-05-15T21:11:25Z`; we remain on 2026.4.22). Decision = **stay 2026.4.22 through Phase 0**; upgrade evaluation is a deliberate post-Phase-0 decision, NOT a mid-session pivot. (Out of scope at 6a.27.)

### M5 — Homebrew core update discipline
- **What:** Homebrew formulae auto-update on `brew update` invocation; the brew binary itself updates similarly.
- **Risk if neglected:** none acutely — brew update is generally safe. **But there's a ceremony-collision risk:** running `brew update` during a state-changing ceremony (F45 gateway restoration, gog upgrade, OpenClaw upgrade, macOS major update) can interact in unexpected ways. Homebrew may decide to update other formulas implicitly that have transitive interactions with the in-progress ceremony.
- **Cadence:** brew update runs implicitly when needed; explicit `brew update` runs are fine on their own (read-only refresh of formulas) but should NOT run during another state-changing ceremony.
- **Treatment:** standing protocol — any state-changing ceremony involving Homebrew (gogcli upgrade, OpenClaw upgrade, future Homebrew Python install for D18, etc.) starts with EITHER an explicit `brew update` immediately before the ceremony OR an explicit `HOMEBREW_NO_AUTO_UPDATE=1` env var to suppress updates during the ceremony. Choice depends on whether you want fresh formulas (then update) or stable formulas (then suppress). Default: suppress during state-changing ceremonies.
- **Owner:** No assigned owner per D19 — M5 is a passive working-protocol rule (apply `HOMEBREW_NO_AUTO_UPDATE=1` during state-changing ceremonies) rather than a tracked recurring item. Future-Claude executing any Homebrew-touching ceremony embeds this protocol; CoS doesn't track it.
- **Status:** STANDING — embed in working protocol for future sessions touching Homebrew.

### M6 — Inert 0.13.0-schema keyring file cleanup (deferred from 6a.20)
- **What:** 2 files at `~/Library/Application Support/gogcli/keyring/token:pfedchen@gmail.com` (1336b) + `token:default:pfedchen@gmail.com` (1346b). Written at 6a.20 Stage 2 OAuth re-grant on 0.13.0; inert under 0.14.0 (schema mismatch); zero operational impact.
- **Risk if neglected:** zero. Files are inert; consume ~3KB; no security risk (encrypted under same `GOG_KEYRING_PASSWORD` as active keyring).
- **Cadence:** no specific cadence; just delete next time the keyring directory is touched for any reason (e.g., during M2 gogcli upgrade ceremony, M3 macOS major-version update, or any future re-grant ceremony).
- **Treatment:** single command: `rm "$HOME/Library/Application Support/gogcli/keyring/token:pfedchen@gmail.com" "$HOME/Library/Application Support/gogcli/keyring/token:default:pfedchen@gmail.com"`. Verify post-delete: 6 keyring files (down from 8); 0.14.0 `auth list` unchanged.
- **Owner:** Peter through 6c, then transfers to Andreas/CoS per D19 as a piggyback-checklist-item attached to M2 / M3 / any future re-grant ceremony. CoS adds the `rm` command to any draft upgrade-ceremony shape that will be touching the keyring directory anyway; opportunistic rather than scheduled.
- **Status:** OPEN, non-blocking, opportunistic cleanup item.

### M7 — Security awareness + recurring hygiene cycle (added 2026-05-05 at Session 6a.23 close)
- **What it is:** Architecture §4.1 specifies a comprehensive recurring security/hygiene posture that wasn't captured in M1-M6 (those covered runtime dependency maintenance — Python deps, gogcli, macOS, OpenClaw, Homebrew, keyring cleanup). Security-specific recurring tasks were carried implicitly until 6a.23 audit surfaced them.
- **Sub-items by cadence:**
  - **Hourly**: jgamblin/OpenClawCVEs tracker monitoring per §4.1 "Staying current" — CVE feed for OpenClaw-specific vulnerabilities; informational-only unless critical CVE surfaces. Workspace self-modification git status check per §4.1 #18 — captured separately under S9 sub-item (3); M7 references.
  - **Daily**: 6am security audit cron per §4.1 #8 + §3.7 — captured under D21 + S9 sub-item (1); M7 references.
  - **Weekly**: `npm outdated -g openclaw` per §4.1 + Monday 6am cron — captured under M4 (OpenClaw updates) at quarterly evaluation level; this M7 sub-item adds the WEEKLY automated check distinct from quarterly evaluation. **Distinction**: weekly = surface-availability check (is there a new release?); quarterly M4 = full evaluation + upgrade ceremony.
  - **Monthly hygiene cycle** per §4.1 "Staying current":
    - Rotate API keys: Anthropic + OpenAI + Brave + GitHub PAT rotated monthly. Replace + 1Password update + verify smoke-tests across all agents. **F25 materialise-once rule applies**: auth-profiles re-materialisation mandatory after every key rotation.
    - Verify OAuth scopes: Gmail + Calendar OAuth scopes per-account checked against architecture-required scopes (gmail.modify, calendar.events). Rotate any unused scope grants.
    - Skills review: review skills-manifest.md against installed skills; verify no unauthorized installations; remove unused.
    - MEMORY.md review: per-agent MEMORY.md sanity check; flag drift / staleness / privacy concerns.
    - OpenClaw Discord security channel review per §4.1 "Staying current" — informational; flag any community-reported critical issues.
  - **Ad-hoc**: Stolen device protocol execution per §4.1 — runbook captured in S7 knowledge base; M7 ensures the runbook stays current.
- **Cadence enforcement:** CoS monthly health report (per S7 Item 4) tracks each M7 cadence cycle's completion; flags any missed cycles to Peter.
- **Treatment:** Each cadence interval, CoS produces a checklist + reminder; Peter executes (Anthropic/OpenAI key rotation requires UI work; Discord review requires reading); CoS updates audit trail in M7's row updates.
- **Owner:** Peter executes ceremonies. CoS tracks cadence + flags reminders + maintains audit trail post-6c per D19 + S7.
- **Status:** OPEN — captured at 6a.23 close as previously-implicit security hygiene cycle made explicit per audit. First cadence cycles begin post-6b launch.
- **Closure path:** never closes; standing discipline like M2-M5.
